produce by papeter mary meehan and the online distribute proofread team the life of hon william f cody know as buffalo bill the famous hunter scout and guide _ a autobiography _ 1879 to general philip h sheridan this book be most respectfully dedicate by the author -lrb- illustration : yours sincerely w f cody -rrb- introductory the life and adventure of hon william f cody -- buffalo bill -- as tell by himself make up a narrative which read more like romance than reality and which in many respects will prove a valuable contribution to the record of we western frontier history while no literary excellence be claim for the narrative it have the greater merit of be truthful and be verify in such a manner that no one can doubt its veracity the frequent reference to such military man as general sheridan carr merritt crook terry colonel royal and other officer under whom mr cody serve as scout and guide at different time and in various section of the frontier during the numerous indian campaign of the last ten or twelve year afford ample proof of he genuineness as a thoroughbred scout there be no humbug or braggadocio about buffalo bill he be know far and wide and he reputation have be earn honestly and by hard work by a combination of circumstance he be educate to the life of a plainsman from he youth up and not the least interesting portion of he career be that of he early life pass as it be in kansa during the eventful and troubleous time connect with the settlement of that state spending much time in the saddle while a mere boy he cross the plain many time in company with bull-train on some of these trip he meet with thrilling adventure and have several hairbreadth escape from death at the hand of indian then for a while he be dash over the plain as a pony-express rider soon afterwards mount on the high seat of a overland stagecoach he be drive a six-in-hand team we next hear of he crack the bull-whacker 's whip and command a wagon-train through a wild and dangerous country to the far west during the civil war he enlist as a private and become a scout with the union army since the war he have be employ as hunter trapper guide scout and actor as a buffalo hunter he have no superior as a trailer of indian he have no equal for many year he have take a active part in all the principal indian campaign on the western frontier and as a scout and guide he have render inestimable service to the various expedition which he accompany during he life on the plain he not only have many exciting adventure himself but he become associate with many of the other note plainsman and in he narrative he frequently refer to they and relate many interesting incident and thrilling event connect with they he have have a fertile field from which to produce this volume and have frequently find it necessary to condense the fact in order to embody the most interesting event of he life the follow from a letter write by general e a carr of the fifth cavalry now command fort mcpherson speak for itself : \* \* \* \* \* i first meet mr cody October 22d 1868 at buffalo station on the kansas pacific railroad in kansas he be scout and guide for the seven company of the fifth cavalry then under colonel royal and of which i be order to take the command from he service with my command steadily in the field for nine month from October 1868 to July 1869 and at subsequent time i be qualify to bear testimony to he quality and character he be very modest and unassuming i do not know for a long time how good a title he have to the appellation ` buffalo bill ' i be apt to discount the claim of scout as they will occasionally exaggerate and when i find one who say nothing about himself i do not think much of he till i have prove he he be a natural gentleman in he manners as well as in character and have none of the roughness of the typical frontiersman he can take he own part when require but i have never hear of he use a knife or a pistol or engage in a quarrel where it could be avoid he personal strength and activity be such that he can hardly meet a man whom he can not handle and he temper and disposition be so good that no one have reason to quarrel with he he eye-sight be better than a good field glass he be the best trailer i ever hear of and also the best judge of the ` lay of country ' -- that be he be able to tell what kind of country be ahead so as to know how to act he be a perfect judge of distance and always ready to tell correctly how many mile it be to water or to any place or how many mile have be march mr cody seem never to tire and be always ready to go in the darkest night or the worst weather and usually volunteer know what the emergency require he trail when follow indian or look for stray animal or game be simply wonderful he be a most extraordinary hunter i could not believe that a man could be certain to shoot antelope run till i have see he do it so often in a fight mr cody be never noisy obstreperous or excite in fact i never hardly notice he in a fight unless i happen to want he or he have something to report when he be always in the right place and he information be always valuable and reliable during the winter of 1868 we encounter hardship and exposure in terrific snow storm sleet etc etc on one occasion that winter mr cody show he quality by quietly offer to go with some dispatch to general sheridan across a dangerous region where another principal scout be reluctant to risk himself on the 13th of may 1869 he be in the fight at elephant rock kansa and trail the indian till the 16th when we get another fight out of they on spring creek in nebraska and scatter they after follow they one hundred and fifty mile in three day it be at spring creek where cody be ahead of the command about three mile with the advance guard of forty man when two hundred indian suddenly surround they we man dismount and form in a circle hold they horse firing and slowly retreat they all to this day speak of cody 's coolness and bravery this be the dog soldier band which capture mr alderdice and mr weichel in kansas they strangle mr alderdice 's baby kill mr weichel 's husband and take a great deal of property and stock from different person we get on they trail again June 28th and follow it nearly two hundred mile till we strike the indian on Sunday July 11th 1869 at summit spring the indian as soon as they see we come kill mr alderdice with a hatchet and shot mr weichel but fortunately not fatally and she be save mr cody have since serve with I as post guide and scout at fort mcpherson where he frequently distinguish himself in the summer of 1876 cody go with I to the black hill region where he kill yellow-hand afterwards he be with the big horn and yellowstone expedition i consider that he service to the country and the army by trail finding and fight indian and thus protect the frontier settler and by guide command over the best and most practicable route have be far beyond the compensation he have receive he friend of the fifth cavalry be all glad that he be in a lucrative business and hope that he may live long and prosper personally i feel under obligation to he for assistance in my campaign which no other man could or would have render of course i wish he and he every success e a carr lt col 5th cav brev maj gen ' l u s army fort mcpherson nebraska July 3d 1878 \* \* \* \* \* buffalo bill be now a actor and be meet with success he own a large and valuable farm adjoining the town of north platte nebraska and there he family live in ease and comfort he have also a extensive cattle ranch on the dismal river sixty-five mile north of north platte he partner be major frank north the old commander of the celebrated pawnee scout while many event of he career be know to the public yet the reader will find in this narrative much that will be entirely new and intensely interesting to both young and old the publisher illustration the author childhood my _ début _ upon the world 's stage occur on February 26th 1845 the scene of this first important event in my adventurous career be in scott county in the state of iowa my parent isaac and mary ann cody who be number among the pioneer of iowa give to I the name of william frederick i be the fourth child in the family martha and julium my sister and samuel my brother have precede I and the child who come after I be eliza nellie mary and charle bear in the order name at the time of my birth the family reside on a farm which they call napsinekee place -- a indian name -- and here the first six or seven year of my childhood be spend when i be about seven year old my father move the family to the little town of leclair located on the bank of the mississippus fifteen mile above the city of davenport even at that early age my adventurous spirit lead I into all sort of mischief and danger and when i look back upon my childhood 's day i often wonder that i do not get drown while swimming or sailing or my neck break while i be steal apple in the neighbor orchard i well remember one day that i go sailing with two other boy in a few minute we find ourselves in the middle of the mississippus become frighten at the situation we lose we presence of mind as well as we oar we at once set up a chorus of pitiful yell when a man who fortunately hear we come to we rescue with a canoe and tow we ashore we have steal the boat and we trouble do not end until we have each receive a merit whipping which impress the incident vividly upon my mind i recollect several occasion when i be nearly eat up by a large and savage dog which act as custodian of a orchard and also of a melon patch which i frequently visit once as i be climb over the fence with a hatful of apple this dog which have start for I catch I by the seat of the pantaloons and while i clung to the top of the fence he literally tear they from my leg but fortunately do not touch my flesh i get away with the apple however by tumble over to the opposite side of the fence with they it be at leclair that i acquire my first experience as a equestrian somehow or other i have manage to corner a horse near a fence and have climb upon he back the next moment the horse get he back up and hoist I into the air i fall violently to the ground striking upon my side in such a way as to severely wrench and strain my arm from the effect of which i do not recover for some time i abandon the art of horsemanship for a while and be induce after considerable persuasion to turn my attention to letter -- my a b c 's -- which be teach I at the village school my father at this time be run a stage line between chicago and davenport no railroad then have be build west of chicago in 1849 he get the californium fever and make up he mind to cross the great plain -- which be then and for year afterwards call the american desert -- to the pacific coast he get ready a complete outfit and start with quite a party after proceed a few mile all but my father and greatly to he disappointment change they mind for some reason and abandon the enterprise they all return home and soon afterwards father move he family out to walnut grove farm in scott county -lrb- illustration : youthful adventure -rrb- while live there i be send to school more for the purpose of be keep out of mischief than to learn anything much of my time be spend in trapping quail which be very plentiful i greatly enjoy study the habit of the little bird and in devise trap to take they in i be most successful with the common figure 4 trap which i could build myself thus i think it be that i acquire my love for hunting i visit the quail trap twice a day morning and evening and as i have now become quite a good rider i be allow to have one of the farm horse to carry I over my route many a jolly ride i have and many a boyish prank be perpetrate after get well away from and out of the sight of home with the horse there be one event which occur in my childhood which i can not recall without a feeling of sadness it be the death of my brother samuel who be accidentally kill in he twelfth year my father at the time be considerable of a politician as well as a farmer be attend a political convention for he be well know in those day as a old line whig he have be a member of the iowa legislature be a justice of the peace and have hold other office he be a excellent stump speaker and be often call upon to canvass the country round about for different candidate the convention which he be attend at the time of the accident be be hold at a cross-road tavern call sherman 's about a mile away samuel and i have go out together on horseback for the cow he ride a vicious mare which mother have tell he time and again not to ride as it have a ugly disposition we be pass the school house just as the child be be dismiss when samuel undertake to give a exhibition of he horsemanship he be a good rider for a boy the mare betsy become unmanageable rear and fall backward upon he injure he internally he be pick up and carry amid great excitement to the house of a neighbor i at once set out with my horse at the top of he speed for my father and inform he of samuel 's mishap he take the horse and return immediately when i arrive at mr burn ' house where my brother be i find my father mother and sister there all weep bitterly at samuel 's bedside a physician after examine he pronounce he injury to be of a fatal character he die the next morning my brother be a great favorite with everybody and he death cast a gloom upon the whole neighborhood it be a great blow to all of the family and especially to father who seem to be almost heart break over it father have be greatly disappoint at the failure of he californium expedition and still desire to move to some new country the death of samuel no doubt increase this desire and he determine to emigrate accordingly early in the spring of 1852 he dispose of he farm and late in march we take we departure for kansa which be then a unsettled territory we outfit consist of one carriage three wagon and some fine blooded horse the carriage be occupy by my mother and sister thus we leave we iowa home -lrb- illustration : samuel 's fatal accident -rrb- father have a brother elijah cody living at weston platte county missourus he be the lead merchant of the place as the town be located near the kansas line father determine to visit he and thither we journey be direct we route lay across iowa and missourus and the trip prove of interest to all of we and especially to I there be something new to be see at nearly every turn of the road at night the family generally put up at hotel or cross-road tavern along the way one day as we be proceed on we way we be meet by a horseman who want to sell he horse or trade-him for another he say the horse have be capture wild in californium that he be a runner and a racer that he have be sell by he different owner on account of he great desire to run away when take part in a race the stranger seem to be very frank in he statement and appear to be very anxious to get rid of the animal and as we be go to kansa where there would be plenty of room for the horse to run as far as he please father conclude to make a trade for he so a exchange of animal be easily and satisfactorily effect the new horse be a small gray we name he little gray a opportunity of test the racing quality of the horse be soon afford one day we drive into a small missourus town or hamlet which lay on we route where the farmer from the surrounding country be congregate for the purpose of have a holiday -- the principal amusement be horse-racing father have no trouble in arrange a race for little gray and select one of he teamster to ride he the missourian match they fastest horse against he and be confident of clean out the emigrant as they call father they be a hard look crowd they wear they pantaloons in they boot they hair be long bushy and untrimmed they face have evidently never make the acquaintance of a razor they seem determine to win the race by fair means or foul they do a great deal of swearing and swagger about in rather a ruffianly style all these incident attract my attention -- everything be new to I -- and become firmly impressed upon my memory my father be unaccustomed to the way of such rough people act very cautiously and as they be all very anxious to bet on they own horse he could not be induce to wager a very large sum on little gray as he be afraid of foul play wa-al now stranger exclaim one of the crowd what kind o ' critter have you get anyhow as how you be afraid to back he up very heavy i 'll bet five to one agin the emergrant 's gray say another i be bet the same way i 'll go yer five hundred dollar agin a hundred that the gray nag git leave behind do i hear any man who want to come agin I on they yer term shout still another hi yer boy give the stranger a chance do not scare he out of he boot say a man who evidently be afraid that my father might back out father have but little to say however and would not venture more than fifty dollar on the result of the race gentleman i be only race my horse for sport say he and be only bet enough to make it interesting i have never see little gray run and therefore do not know what he can do at the same time he be confident that he horse would come in the winner as he have choose a excellent rider for he finally all the preliminary of the contest be arrange the judge be choose and the money be deposit in the hand of a stake-holder the race be to be a single dash of a mile the horse be bring side by side and mount by they rider at the signal -- one two three go -- off they start like a flash the missouri horse take the lead for the first quarter of a mile at the half-mile however he begin to weaken the missourian shout themselves hoarse in urge they horse but all to no avail the little gray pass he and continue to leave he farther and farther behind easily win the race the affair create a great deal of enthusiasm but the race be conduct with honor and fairness which be quite a agreeable surprise to my father who soon find the missourian to be at heart very clever man -- thus show that outside appearance be sometimes very deceptive they nearly all come up and congratulate he on he success ask he why he have not bet more money on the race and want to buy little gray gentleman say he when i drive up here and arrange for this race i feel confident that my horse would win it i be among entire stranger and therefore i only bet a small amount i be afraid that you would cheat I in some way or other i see now that i be mistake as i have find you to be honorable man wa-all you could have break _ I _ say the man who want to bet the five hundred dollar to one hundred for that there nag o ' yourn look no more like a runner nor i do during we stay in the place they treat we very kindly and continue to try to purchase little gray my father however remain firm in he determination not to part with he the next place of interest which we reach after resume we journey be within twenty mile of weston we have be stop at farm house along the road and could not get anything to eat in the shape of bread except corn bread of which all have become heartily tire as we be drive along we see in the distance a large and handsome brick residence father say : they probably have white bread there we drive up to the house and learn that it be own and occupy by mr burn mother of a well-known lawyer of that name who be now live in leavenworth she be a wealthy lady and give we to understand in a pleasant way that she do not entertain traveler my father in the course of the conversation with she say : do you know elijah cody indeed i do say she he frequently visit we and we visit he we be the best of friend he be a brother of mine say father be it possible she exclaim why you must remain here all night have you family come into the house at once you must not go another step today the kind invitation be accept and we remain there over night as father have predict we find plenty of white bread at this house and it prove quite a luxurious treat my curiosity be considerably arouse by the many negro which i see about the premise as i have scarcely ever see any colored people the few be on the steamboat as they pass up and down the mississippus river the next day my father and mother drive over to weston in a carriage and return with my uncle elijah we then all proceed to he house and as kansa be not yet open for settlement as a territory we remain there a few day while father cross over into kansa on a prospect tour he visit the kickapoo agency -- five mile above weston -- on the kansas side of the missourus river he become acquaint with the agent and make arrangement to establish himself there as a indian trader he then return to weston and located the family on one of elijah cody 's farm three mile from town where we be to remain until kansa should be throw open for settlement after complete these arrangement he establish a trading post at salt creek valley in kansas four mile from the kickapoo agency one day after he have be absent some little time he come home and say that he have buy two pony for I and that next morning he would take I over into kansa this be pleasant news as i have be very anxious to go there with he and the fact that i be now the owner of two pony make I feel very proud that night i could not sleep a wink in the morning i be up long before the sun and after a early breakfast father and i start out on we trip cross the missourus river at the rialto ferry we land in kansa and pass along to fort leavenworth four mile distant chapter ii early influence general harney be in command at fort leavenworth at the time of we visit and a regiment of cavalry be station there they be have a dress parade when we ride up and as this be the first time that i have ever see any soldier i think it be a grand sight i shall never forget it especially the maneuver on horseback after witness the parade we resume we journey on the way to my father 's trading camp we have to cross over a high hill know as salt creek hill from the top of which we look down upon the most beautiful valley i have ever see it be about twelve mile long and five mile wide the different tributary of salt creek come down from the range of hill at the southwest at the foot of the valley another small river -- plum creek also flow the bluff fringe with tree clothe in they full foliage add greatly to the picturesqueness of the scene while this beautiful valley greatly interested I yet the most novel sight of a entirely different character which meet my enraptured gaze be the vast number of white-covered wagon or prairie-schooner which be encamp along the different stream i ask my father what they be and where they be go he explain to I that they be emigrant wagon bind for utah and californium at that time the mormon and californium trail run through this valley which be always select as a camping place there be at least one thousand wagon in the valley and they white cover lend a please contrast to the green grass the cattle be quietly grazing near the wagon while the emigrant be either rest or attend to camp duty a large number of the wagon as i learn from my father belong to major & russell the great government freighter they have several train there each consist of twenty-five wagon heavily load with government supplies they be all camp and corrale in a circle while we be view this scene a long wagon train come pull up the hill bind out from fort leavenworth to some distant frontier post the cattle be wild and the man be whipping they fearfully the loud report of the bull-whip sound like gun-shot they be doubling-up and some of the wagon be be draw by fifteen yoke of ox i remember ask my father a great many question and he explain to I all about the freighting business across the great plain and tell I about the different government post point over to the army of wagon camp below we he show I which be the mormon ' and which be the californian ' and say that we must steer clear of the former as the cholera be rage among they five hundred have die that spring -- 1853 -- and the grave-yard be daily increase its dimension the unfortunate people have be overtake by the dreadful disease and have be compel to halt on they journey until it abate while we be look at the mormon they be hold a funeral service over the remains of some of they number who have die they old cemetery be yet indicate by various land-mark which however with the few remain head-board be fast disappear we pass on through this valley of death as it might then have be very appropriately call and after ride for some time my father point out a large hill and show I he camp which afterwards become we home there be another trading-post near by which be conduct by mr mp rively who have a store build partly frame and partly of log we stop at this establishment for a while and find perhaps a hundred man woman and child gather there engage in trading and gossip the man have huge pistol and knife in they belt they pantaloons be tuck in they boot and they wear large broad-rimmed hat to I they appear like a lot of cut-throat pirate who have come ashore for a lark it be the first time i have ever see man carry pistol and knife and they look like a very dangerous crowd some be buy article of merchandise other be talk about the cholera the various camp and matter of interest while other be drink whisky freely and become intoxicate it be a busy and a exciting scene and rively appear to be do a rush trade at some little distance from the store i notice a small party of dark-skinned and rather fantastically dress people whom i ascertain be indian and as i have never before see a real live indian i be much interested in they i go over and endeavor to talk to they but we conversation be very limited that evening we reach we camp which be located two mile west of rively 's the first thing i do be to hunt up my pony and from my father 's description of they i have no difficulty in find they they be lariate in the grass and i immediately run up to they suppose they to be gentle animal i be greatly mistaken however as they snort and jump away from I and would not allow I to come near they my father who be stand not far distant inform I that the pony be not yet broken i be somewhat disappoint at this and thereupon he and one of he man catch one of the animal and bridle she then put I on she back lead she around greatly to my delight i keep pet she so much that she soon allow I to approach she she be a beautiful bay and i name she dolly the other pony be a sorrel and i call he prince in the evening some indian visit the camp -- which as yet consist only of tent though some log have be cut preparatory to build house -- and exchange they fur for clothing sugar and tobacco father have not learn they language and therefore communicate with they by means of sign we have we supper by the camp-fire and that night be the first time i ever camp out and sleep upon the ground the day have be a eventful one to I for all the incident be full of excitement and romance to my youthful mind and i think no apology be need for mention so many of the little circumstance which so greatly interested I in my childhood 's day and which no doubt have a great influence in shape my course in after year my love of hunting and scout and life on the plain generally be the result of my early surroundings the next morning father visit the kickapoo agency take I along he ride a horse and put I on my pony dolly lead the animal all the way he seem anxious to break I in as well as the pony and i greatly enjoy this my first day 's ride on a kansas prairie at the kickapoo village i see hundred of indian some of whom be live in lodge but the majority occupy log cabin the agent reside in a double-hewed log house one of the apartment of which be use as a school for the indian the agency store be opposite this structure all the building be whitewashed and look neat and clean the kickapoo be very friendly indian and we spend much of we time among they look about and study they habit after a while we return to we own camp and just as we arrive there we see a drive of horse -- there be three or four hundred in all -- approach from the west over the californium trail they be be drive by seven or eight mount man wear sombrero and dress in buckskin with they lariat dangle from they saddle and they be follow by two or three pack-mule or horse they go into camp a little below we on the bank of the stream presently one of the man walk out towards we camp and my father call to I to come and see a genuine western man he be about six foot two inch tall be well build and have a light springy and wiry step he wear a broad-brimmed californium hat and be dress in a complete suit of buckskin beautifully trim and bead he salute we and father invite he to sit down which he do after a californian yes i reply and one of they never have be ridden well i 'll ride he for you and spring lightly to he foot he continue : come on where be the animal accordingly we all go to the place where prince be lariate the stranger untie the rope from the picket pin and take a half-loop around the pony 's nose he jump on he back in a moment he be fly over the prairie the untame steed rearing and pitch every once in a while in he effort to throw he rider but the man be not unseated he be evidently a experienced horseman i watch he every movement i be unconsciously take another lesson in the practical education which have serve I so well through my life the californian ride the pony until it be completely master then come up to I jump to the ground hand I the rope and say : here 's you pony he be all right now i lead prince away while father and the stranger sit down in the shade of a tent and begin talk about the latter 's horsemanship which father consider very remarkable oh that be nothing i be raise on horseback say the californian i run away from home when a boy go to sea and finally land in the sandwich island where i fall in with a circus with which i remain two year during that time i become a celebrated bare-back rider i then go to californium be attract there by the gold excitement the news of which have reach the island i do not go to mine however but go to work as a _ bocarro _ - catch and break wild horse great number of which be roam through california last summer we catch this herd that we have bring with we across the plain and be take it to the state to sell i come with the outfit as it give I a good opportunity to visit my relative who live at cleveland ohio i also have a uncle over at weston across the river when i run away and to-morrow i be go to visit the town to see if he be there yet -lrb- illustration : billing as a bocarro -rrb- i be acquaint in weston say father and perhaps i can tell you about you uncle what be he name elijah billing have never be hear of from the day he run away from home and he relative have frequently wonder what have become of he he appearance therefore in we camp in the guise of a californian be have stampede from fort leavenworth and between two and three hundred of the horse be run at large over the kansas prairie and have become quite wild a reward of ten dollar be offer for every one of the horse that be capture and deliver to the quartermaster at fort leavenworth this kind of work of course just suit the roaming disposition of billing especially as it be similar to that in which he have be engage in californium the horse have to be catch with a lasso with which he be very expert he borrow little gray who be fleet enough for the wildest of the runaway and then he at once begin he bidding we all good-bye start for salt lake drive six yoke of oxen chapter iii boy day in kansa during the summer of 1853 we live in we little log house and father continue to trade with the indian who become very friendly hardly a day pass without a social visit from they i spend a great deal of time with the indian boy who teach I how to shoot with the bow and arrow at which i become quite expert i also take part in all they sport and learn to talk the kickapoo language to some extent father desire to express he friendship for these indian and accordingly arrange a grand barbecue for they he invite they all to be present on a certain day which they be he then present they with two fat beef to be kill and cook in the various indian style mother make several large boiler full of coffee which she give to they together with sugar and bread there be about two hundred indian in attendance at the feast and they all enjoy and appreciate it in the evening they have one of they grand entertainment the indian return to they home well satisfied my uncle at that time own a trading post at silver lake in the pottawattamie country on the kansas river and he arrange a excursion to that place among the party be several lady from weston and father mother and myself mr mcmeekan my uncle 's superintendent who have come to weston for supplies conduct the party to the post the trip across the prairie be a delightful one and we remain at the post several day father and one or two of the man go on to fort riley to view the country and upon they return my uncle entertain the pottawattamie indian with a barbecue similar to the one give by father to the kickapoo during the latter part of the summer father fill a hay contract at fort leavenworth i pass much of my time among the camper and spend day and day in ride over the country with mr william russell who be engage in the freighting business and who seem to take a considerable interest in I in this way i become acquaint with many wagon-master hunter and teamster and learn a great deal about the business of handle cattle and mule it be a excellent school for I and i acquire a great deal of practical knowledge which afterwards i find to be of invaluable service for it be not long before i become employ by major & russell remain with they in different capacity for several year the winter of 1853-54 be spend by father at we little prairie home in cut house log and fence rail which he intend to use on he farm as soon as the bill for the opening of the territory for settlement should pass this bill which be call the enable act of kansas territory be pass in April 1854 and father immediately pre-empt the claim on which we be live the summer of that year be a exciting period in the history of the new territory thousand and thousand of people seek new home flock thither a large number of the emigrant come over from adjoining state the missourian some of they would come laden with bottle of whisky and after drink the liquor would drive the bottle into the ground to mark they land claim not wait to put up any building the missourian mostly be pro-slavery man and hold enthusiastic meeting at which they express they desire that kansa should be a slave state and do not hesitate to declare they determination to make it so rively 's store be the headquarters for these man and there they hold they meeting -lrb- illustration : stake out lot -rrb- at first they think father would coincide with they on account of he brother elijah be a missourian but in this they be greatly mistake at one of they gathering when there be about one hundred of the reckless man present my father who happen also to be there be call upon for a speech after considerable urge he mount the box and begin speak as nearly as i can recollect as follow : gentleman and fellow-citizen : you have call upon I for a speech and i have accept you invitation rather against my will as my view may not accord with the sentiment of the rest of this assembly my remark at this time will be brief and to the point the question before we to-day be shall the territory of kansas be a free or a slave state the question of slavery in itself be a broad one and one which i do not care at this time and place to discuss at length i apprehend that you motive in call upon I be to have I express my sentiment in regard to the introduction of slavery into kansas i shall gratify you wish in that respect i be one of the pioneer of the state of iowa and aid in its settlement when it be a territory and help to organize it as a state gentleman i vote that it should be a _ white _ state -- that negro whether free or slave should never be allow to locate within its limit and gentleman i say to you now and i say it boldly that i propose to exert all my power in make kansa the same kind of a state as iowa i believe in let slavery remain as it now exist and i shall always oppose its further extension these be my sentiment gentleman and let I tell you -- he never finish this sentence or he speech he expression be anything but acceptable to the rough-looking crowd whose ire have be gradually rise to fever heat and at this point they hoot and hiss he and shout you black abolitionist shut up get down from that box kill he shoot he and so on father however maintain he position on the dry-goods box notwithstanding the excitement and the numerous invitation to step down until a hot-headed pro-slavery man who be in the employ of my uncle elijah crowd up and say : get off that box you black abolitionist or i 'll pull you off father pay but little attention to he and attempt to resume he speech intend doubtless to explain he position and endeavor to somewhat pacify the angry crowd but the fellow jump up on the box and pull out a huge bowie knife stab father twice who reel and fall to the ground the man spring after he and would have end he life then and there have not some of the better man in the crowd interfere in time to prevent he from carry out he murderous intention the excitement be intense and another assault would probably have be make on my father have not rively hurriedly carry he to he home there be no doctor within any reasonable distance and father at once request that he be convey in the carriage to he brother elijah 's house in weston my mother and a driver accordingly go there with he where he wound be dress he remain in weston several week before he be able to stir about again but he never fully recover from the wound which eventually prove the cause of he death -lrb- illustration : my father stab -rrb- my uncle of course at once discharge the ruffian from he employ the man afterwards become a note desperado and be quite conspicuous in the kansas war my father 's indiscreet speech at rively 's bring upon we family all of the misfortune and difficulty which from that time on befall we as soon as he be able to attend to he business again the missourian begin to harass he in every possible way and keep it up with hardly a moment 's cessation kickapoo city as it be call a small town that have spring into existence seven mile up the river from fort leavenworth become the hot-bed of the pro-slavery doctrine and the headquarters of its advocate here be really the beginning of the kansas trouble my father who have shed the first blood in the cause of the freedom of kansa be notify upon he return to he trading post to leave the territory and he be threaten with death by hang or shoot if he dare to remain -lrb- illustration : my father 's escape -rrb- one night a body of armed man mount on horse ride up to we house and surround it know what they have come for and see that there would be but little chance for he in a encounter with they father determine to make he escape by a little stratagem hastily disguise himself in mother 's bonnet and shawl he boldly walk out of the house and proceed towards the corn-field the darkness prove a great protection as the horseman between whom he pass be unable to detect he in he disguise suppose he to be a woman they neither halt he nor follow he and he pass safely on into the corn-field where he conceal himself the horseman soon dismount and inquire for father mother very truthfully tell they that he be away they be not satisfy with she statement however and they at once make a thorough search of the house they rave and swear when they could not find he and threaten he with death whenever they should catch he i be sure if they have capture he that night they would have kill he they carry off nearly everything of value in the house and about the premise then go to the pasture they drive off all the horse my pony prince afterward succeed in break away from they and come back home father lay not dare to follow he while he be stay at fort leavenworth he hear that jim lane captain cleveland and captain chandler be on they way from indiana to kansa with a body of free state man between two and three hundred strong they be to cross the missourus river near doniphan between leavenworth and nebraska city they destination be lawrence father determine to join they and take passage on a steamboat which be go up the river have reach the place of cross he make himself know to the leader of the party by whom he be most cordially receive the pro-slavery man hearing of the approach of the free state party resolve to drive they out of the territory the two party meet at hickory point where a severe battle be fight several be kill the victory result in favor of the free state man who pass on to lawrence without much further opposition my father finally leave they and see that he could no longer live at home go to grasshopper fall thirty-five mile west of leavenworth there he begin the erection of a saw-mill while he be thus engage we learn from one of we hire workman at home that the pro-slavery man have lay another plan to kill he and be on they way to grasshopper fall to carry out they intention mother at once start I off on prince to warn father of the come danger when i have go about seven mile i suddenly come upon a party of man who be camp at the cross of stranger creek as i pass along i hear one of they who recognize I say that be the son of the old abolitionist we be after and the next moment i be command to halt -lrb- illustration : life or death -rrb- instead of stop i instantly start my pony on a run and on look back i see that i be be pursue by three or four of the party who have mount they horse no doubt suppose that they could easily capture I it be very fortunate that i have hear the remark about my be the son of the abolitionist for then i know in a instant that they be _ en route _ to grasshopper fall to murder my father i at once see the importance of my escape and warn father in time it be a matter of life or death to he so i urge prince to he utmost speed feeling that upon he and myself depend a human life -- a life that be dearer to I than that of any other man in the world i lead my pursuer a lively chase for four or five mile finally when they see they could not catch I they return to they camp i keep straight on to grasshopper fall arrive there in ample time to inform he of the approach of he old enemy that same night father and i ride to lawrence which have become the headquarters of the free state man there he in the most secret manner virtually carry he life in he hand in the spring of this year -lrb- 1855 -rrb- a pro-slavery party come to we house to search for father not find he they depart take with they my pony prince i shall never forget the man who steal that pony he afterwards rise from the low level of a horse thief to the high dignity of a justice of the peace and i think still live at kickapoo the loss of my faithful pony nearly break my heart and bankrupt I in business as i have nothing to ride one day soon afterwards i meet my old friend mr russell to whom i related all my trouble and he generous heart be touch by my story billy my boy say he cheer up and come to leavenworth and i 'll employ you i 'll give you twenty-five dollar a month to herd cattle i accept the offer and heartily thank he hurry home to obtain mother 's consent she refuse to let I go and all my plead be in vain young as i be -- be then only in my tenth year my idea and knowledge of the world however be far in advance of my age -- i determine to run away from home mr russell 's offer of twenty-five dollar a month be a temptation which i could not resist the remuneration for my service seem very large to I and i accordingly steal away and walk to leavenworth mr badger one of mr russell 's superintendent immediately send I out mount on a little gray mule to herd cattle i work at this for two month and then come into leavenworth i have not be home during all this time but mother have learn from mr russell where i be and she no longer feel uneasy as he have advise she to let I remain in he employ he assure she that i be all right and say that when the herd come in he would allow I to make a visit home upon my arrival in leavenworth with the herd of cattle mr russell instruct he book-keeper mr byer to pay I my wages amount to fifty dollar byer give I the sum all in half-dollar piece i put the bright silver coin into a sack which i tie to my mule and start home think myself a _ millionaire _ this money i give to mother who have already forgive I for run away thus begin my service for the firm of russell & major afterwards russell major & waddell with whom i spend seven year of my life in different capacity -- such as cavallard-driver wagon-master pony express rider and driver i continue to work for mr russell during the rest of the summer of 1855 and in the winter of 1855-56 i attend school father who still continue to secretly visit home be anxious to have he child receive as much of a education as possible under the adverse circumstance surround we and he employ a teacher miss jennie lyon to come to we house and teach my mother be well educate -- more so than my father -- and it use to worry she a great deal because she child could not receive better educational advantage however the little school at home get along exceedingly well and we all make rapid advance in we study as miss lyon be a excellent teacher she afterwards marry a gentleman name hook who become the first mayor of cheyenne where she now live the kansas trouble reach they highest pitch in the spring of 1856 and we family continue to be harass as much as ever by we old enemy i can not now recollect one-half of the serious difficulty that we have to encounter but i very distinctly remember one incident well worth relate i come home one night on a visit from leavenworth be accompany by a fellow-herder -- a young man during the night we hear a noise outside of the house and soon the dog begin bark loudly we look out to ascertain the cause of the disturbance and see that the house be surround by a party of man mother have become accustomed to such occurrence and on this occasion she seem to be master of the situation from the start open a window she coolly sing out in a firm tone of voice : who be you what do you want here we be after that old abolition husband of yours be the answer from one of the crowd he be not in this house and have not be here for a long time say my mother that be a lie we know he be in the house and we be bind to have he say the spokesman of the party i afterwards learn they have mistake the herder who have ride home with I for my father for whom they have be watch my husband be not at home emphatically repeat my heroic mother -- for if there ever be a heroine she certainly be one -- but the house be full of armed man continue she and i 'll give you just two minute to get out of the yard if you be not out by the end of that time i shall order they to fire on you she withdraw from the window for a few moment and hurriedly instruct the herder to call aloud certain name -- any that he might think of -- just as if the house be full of man to whom he be give order he follow she direction to the very letter he could not have do it any better have he rehearse the act a dozen time the party outside hear he as it be intend they should and they suppose that my mother really have quite a force at she command while this little by play be be enact she step to the open window again and say : john green you and you friend have better go away or the man will surely fire on you at this point the herder myself and my sister commence stamp on the floor in imitation of a squad of soldier and the herder issue he order in a loud voice to he imaginary troops who be apparently approach the window preparatory to firing a volley at the enemy this little stratagem prove eminently successful the cowardly villain begin retreat and then my mother fire a old gun into the air which greatly accelerate they speed cause they to break and run they soon disappear from view in the darkness the next morning we accidentally discover that they have intend to blow up the house upon go into the cellar which have be leave open on one side we find two keg of powder together with a fuse secrete there it only require a light match to have send we into eternity my mother 's presence of mind which have never yet desert she in any try situation have save we life shortly after this affair i come home again on a visit and find father there sick with fever and confine to he bed one day my old enemy ride up to the house on my pony prince which he have steal from I what be you business here to-day ask mother i be look for the old man he reply i be go to search the house and if i find he i be go to kill he here you girl say he address my sister get I some dinner and get it quick too for i be as hungry as a wolf very well pray be seat and we 'll get you something to eat say one of my sister without exhibit the least sign of fear he sit down and while they be prepare a dinner for he he take out a big knife and sharpen it on a whetstone repeat he threat of search the house and kill my father i have witness the whole proceeding and hear the threat and i determine that the man should never go up stair where father be lie in bed unable to rise take a double-barreled pistol which i have recently buy i go to the head of the stair cock the weapon and wait for the ruffian to come up determine that the moment he set foot on the step i would kill he i be relieved however from the stern necessity as he do not make he appearance the brute be considerably intoxicate when he come to the house and the longer he sit still the more he brain become muddle with liquor and he actually forget what he have come there for after he have eat he dinner he mount he horse and ride off and it be a fortunate thing for he that he do father soon recover and return to grasshopper fall while i resume my cattle herd chapter iv youthful experience in July 1856 the people live in the vicinity of we home -- feel the necessity of more extensive educational facility for they child than they have yet have -- start a subscription school in a little log cabin on the bank of the creek which for a while prove quite a success my mother be very anxious to have I attend this school i accede to she oft-repeated wish and return home i become a pupil of the institution i make considerable progress in my study -- such as they be -- and be get along very well in every other respect until i become involve in my first love affair like all school-boy i have a sweetheart with whom i be dead in love -- in a juvenile way she name be mary hyatt of course i have a rival stephen gobel a boy about three year my senior -- the bully of the school he be terribly jealous and seek in every way to revenge himself upon I for have win the childish affection of sweet little mary the boy of the school use to build play-house or arbor among the tree and bush for they sweetheart i have build a play-house for mary when steve as we call he level it to the ground we immediately have a very lively fight in which i get badly beat the teacher hear of we quarrel and whip we both this make matter worse than ever as i have receive two thrashing to steve 's one i smother my angry feeling as much as possible under the humiliating circumstance and during the afternoon recess build another play-house think that gobel would not dare to destroy a second one but i be mistake for he push the whole structure over at the first opportunity i come up to he just as he finish the job and say : steve gobel the next time you do that i 'll hurt you and i mean it too but he laugh and call I name -lrb- illustration : two to one -rrb- at recess next morning i begin the construction of still another playhouse and when i have it about two-third finish steve slyly sneak up to the spot and tip the whole thing over i jump for he with the quickness of a cat and clutch he by the throat for a moment i have the advantage of he but he be too strong for I and soon have I on the ground and be beat I severely while away from home i have someway come into possession of a very small pocket dagger which i have carry about with I in its sheath use it in place of a knife during the struggle this fall from my pocket and my hand by accident rest upon it as it lay upon the ground exasperate beyond measure at steve 's persistence in destroy my play-house and smart under he blow i forget myself for the moment grasp the dagger and unthinkingly thrust it into steve 's thigh have it be larger it would probably have injure he severely as it be it make a small wound sufficient to cause the blood to flow freely and steve to cry out in affright : i be kill o i be kill the school child all rush to the spot and be terrify at the scene what be the matter ask one bill cody have kill steve gobel reply another the uproar reach the teacher 's ear and i now see he approach with vengeance in he eye and a big club in he hand i know that he be come to interview _ I _ i be dreadfully frighten at what i have do and undecided whether to run away or to remain and take the consequence but the sight of that flag-staff in the school teacher 's hand be too much for I i no longer hesitate but start off like a deer the teacher follow in hot pursuit but soon become convinced that he could not catch I and give up the chase i keep on run until i reach one of russell major & waddell 's freight train which i have notice go over the hill for the west fortunately for I i know the wagon-master john willis and as soon as i recover my breath i tell he what have happen serve he right billy say he and what be more we 'll go over and clean out the teacher oh no do not do that say i for i be afraid that i might fall into the hand of the wounded boy 's friend who i know would soon be look for I well billy come along with I i be bind for fort kearney the trip will take I forty day i want you for a cavallard driver all right i reply but i must go home and tell mother about it and get some clothes well then to-night after we make we camp i 'll go back with you the affray break up the school for the rest of the day as the excitement be too much for the child late in the afternoon after the train have move on some considerable distance i see steve 's father he brother frank and one of the neighbor rapidly approach mr willi there come old gobel with frank and somebody else and they be after I -- what be i go to do i ask let 'em come say he they can not take you if i have get anything to say about it and i rather think i have get into one of the wagon -- keep quiet and lay low i 'll manage this little job do not you fret a bit about it i obey he order and feel much easier old gobel frank and the neighbor soon come up and inquire for I he be around here somewhere say mr willi we want he say gobel he stab my son a little while ago and i want to arrest he well you can not get he that settle it so you need not waste any of you time around here say willi gobel continue to talk for a few minute but get no greater satisfaction the trio return home when night come willi accompany I on horseback to my home mother who have anxiously search for I everywhere -- be afraid that something have befall I at the hand of the gobel -- be delighted to see I notwithstanding the difficulty in which i have become involved i at once tell she that at present i be afraid to remain at home and have accordingly make up my mind to absent myself for a few week or month -- at least until the excitement should die out mr willi say to she that he would take I to fort kearney with he and see that i be properly care for and would bring I back safely in forty day mother at first seriously object to my go on this trip fear i would fall into the hand of indian she fear however be soon overcome and she conclude to let I go she fix I up a big bundle of clothing and give I a quilt kiss she and my sister a fond farewell i start off on my first trip across the plain and with a light heart too notwithstanding my trouble of a few hour before the trip prove a most enjoyable one to I although no incident worthy of note occur on the way on my return from fort kearney i be pay off the same as the rest of the employee the remainder of the summer and fall i spend in herd cattle and work for russell major & waddell i finally venture home -- not without some fear however of the gobel family -- and be delighted to learn that during my absence mother have have a interview with mr gobel and have settle the difficulty with he the two family have become friend again and i may state incidentally that they ever after remain so i have since often meet stephen gobel and we have have many a laugh together over we love affair and the affray at the school-house mary hyatt the innocent cause of the whole difficulty be now marry and live in chicago thus end my first love scrape in the winter of 1856-57 my father in company with a man name jc bole go to cleveland ohio and organize a colony of about thirty family whom they bring to kansa and located on the grasshopper several of these family still reside there it be during this winter that father after he return from cleveland catch a severe cold this in connection with the wound he have receive at rively 's -- from which he have never entirely recover -- affect he seriously and in April 1857 he die at home from kidney disease this sad event leave my mother and the family in poor circumstance and i determine to follow the plain for a livelihood for they and myself i have no difficulty in obtain work under my old employer and in may 1857 i start for salt lake city with a herd of beef cattle in charge of frank and bill mccarthy for general albert sidney johnson 's army which be then be send across the plain to fight the mormon nothing occur to interrupt we journey until we reach plum creek on the south platte river thirty-five mile west of old fort kearney we have make a morning drive and have camp for dinner the wagon-master and a majority of the man have go to sleep under the mess wagon the cattle be be guard by three man and the cook be prepare dinner no one have any idea that indian be anywhere near we the first warning we have that they be infest that part of the country be the firing of shot and the whoop and yell from a party of they who catch we nap give we a most unwelcome surprise all the man jump to they foot and seize they gun they see with astonishment the cattle run in every direction they have be stampede by the indian who have shoot and kill the three man who be on day-herd duty and the red devil be now charge down upon the rest of we i then think of mother 's fear of my fall into the hand of the indian and i have about make up my mind that such be to be my fate but when i see how coolly and determinedly the mccarthy brother be conduct themselves and give order to the little band i become convinced that we would stand the indian off as the say be we man be all well arm with colt 's revolver and mississippus yager which last carry a bullet and two buckshot the mccarthy boy at the proper moment give order to fire upon the advance enemy the volley check they although they return the compliment and shoot one of we party through the leg frank mccarthy then sing out boy make a break for the slough yonder and we can then have the bank for a breast-work -lrb- illustration : kill my first indian -rrb- we make a run for the slough which be only a short distance off and succeed in safely reach it bring with we the wounded man the bank prove to be a very effective breast-work afford we good protection we have be there but a short time when frank mccarthy see that the longer we be corrale the worse it would be for we say : well boy we 'll try to make we way back to fort kearney by wade in the river and keep the bank for a breast-work we all agree that this be the best plan and we accordingly proceed down the river several mile in this way manage to keep the indian at a safe distance with we gun until the slough make a junction with the main platte river from there down we find the river at time quite deep and in order to carry the wounded man along with we we construct a raft of pole for he accommodation and in this way he be transport occasionally the water would be too deep for we to wade and we be oblige to put we weapon on the raft and swim the indian follow we pretty close and be continually watch for a opportunity to get a good range and give we a rake fire cover ourselves by keep well under the bank we push ahead as rapidly as possible and make pretty good progress the night find we still on the way and we enemy still on we track i be the youngest and smallest of the party become somewhat tired and without notice it i have fall behind the other for some little distance it be about ten o'clock and we be keep very quiet and hug close to the bank when i happen to look up to the moon-lit sky and see the plumed head of a indian peeping over the bank instead of hurry ahead and alarming the man in a quiet way i instantly aim my gun at the head and fire the report ring out sharp and loud on the night air and be immediately follow by a indian whoop and the next moment about six foot of dead indian come tumble into the river i be not only overcome with astonishment but be badly scare as i could hardly realize what i have do i expect to see the whole force of indian come down upon we while i be stand thus bewilder the man who have hear the shot and the war-whoop and have see the indian take a tumble come rush back who fire that shot cry frank mccarthy i do reply i rather proudly as my confidence return and i see the man come up yes and little billy have kill a indian stone-dead -- too dead to skin say one of the man who have approach nearer than the rest and have almost stumble upon the corpse from that time forward i become a hero and a indian killer this be of course the first indian i have ever shoot and as i be not then more than eleven year of age my exploit create quite a sensation the other indian upon learn what have happen to they advance guard set up a terrible howling and fire several volley at we but without do any injury as we be so well protect by the bank we resume we journey down the river and travel all night long just before daylight frank mccarthy crawl out over the bank and discover that we be only five mile from fort kearney which post we reach in safety in about two hour -- shortly after _ reveille _ -- bring the wounded man with we it be indeed a relief to we all to feel that once more we be safe frank mccarthy immediately report to the commanding officer and inform he of all that have happen the commandant at once order a company of cavalry and one of infantry to proceed to plum creek on a forced march -- take a howitzer with they -- to endeavor to recapture the cattle from the indian the firm of russell major & waddell have a division agent at kearney and this agent mount we on mule so that we could accompany the troops on reach the place where the indian have surprise we we find the body of the three man whom they have kill and scalp and literally cut into piece we of course bury the remains we catch but few of the cattle the most of they have be drive off and stampede with the buffalo there be numerous immense herd of the latter in that section of the country at that time the indian 's trail be discover run south towards the republican river and the troops follow it to the head of plum creek and there abandon it return to fort kearney without have see a single red-skin the company 's agent see that there be no further use for we in that vicinity -- as we have lose we cattle and mule -- send we back to fort leavenworth the company it be proper to state do not have to stand the loss of the expedition as the government hold itself responsible for such depredation by the indian on the day that i get into leavenworth sometime in July i be interview for the first time in my life by a newspaper reporter as i then think on the highest pinnacle of fame be john hutchinson and i feel very grateful to he he now live in wichita kansa chapter v in business in the summer of 1857 russell major & waddell be matter of interest to the general reader it may be well in this connection to give a brief description of a freight train the wagon use in those day by russell major & waddell be know as the j murphy wagon make at st loui specially for the plain business they be very large and be strongly build be capable of carry seven thousand pound of freight each the wagon-box be very commodious -- be as large as the room of a ordinary house -- and be cover with two heavy canvas sheet to protect the merchandise from the rain these wagon be generally send out from leavenworth each load with six thousand pound of freight and each draw by several yoke of ox in charge of one driver a train consist of twenty-five wagon all in charge of one man who be know as the wagon-master the second man in command be the assistant wagon-master then come the extra hand next the night herder and lastly the cavallard driver whose duty it be to drive the lame and loose cattle there be thirty-one man all tell in a train the man do they own cooking be divide into mess of seven one man cook another bring wood and water another stand guard and so on each have some duty to perform while get meal all be heavily arm with colt 's pistol and mississippus yager and every one always have he weapon handy so as to be prepare for any emergency the wagon-master in the language of the plain be call the bull-wagon boss the teamster be know as bull-whacker and the whole train be denominate a bull-outfit everything at that time be call a outfit the man of the plain be always full of droll humor and exciting story of they own experience and many a hour i spend in listen to the recital of thrilling adventure and hair-breadth escape russell major & waddell have in they employ two hundred and fifty train compose of 6250 wagon 75000 ox and about eight thousand man they business reach to all the government frontier post in the north and west to which they transport supplies and they also carry freight as far south as new mexico -lrb- illustration : a prairie schooner -rrb- the trail to salt lake run through kansa to the northwest cross the big blue river then over the big and little sandy come into nebraska near the big sandy the next stream of any importance be the little blue along which the trail run for sixty mile then cross a range of sand-hill and strike the platte river ten mile below old fort kearney thence the course lay up the south platte to the old ash hollow cross thence eighteen mile across to the north platte -- near the mouth of the blue water where general harney have he great battle in 1855 with the sioux and cheyenne indian from this point the north platte be follow pass court house rock chimney rock and scott 's bluff and then on to fort laramie where the laramie river be cross still follow the north platte for some considerable distance the trail cross this river at old richard 's bridge and follow it up to the celebrated red butte -- cross the willow creek to the sweet water pass the great independence rock and the devil 's gate up to the three crossing of the sweet water thence past the cold spring where three foot under the sod on the hottest day of summer ice can be find thence to the hot spring and the rocky ridge and through the rocky mountain and echo cañon and thence on to the great salt lake valley we have start on we trip with everything in good shape follow the above describe trail during the first week or two out i become well acquaint with most of the train man and with one in particular who become a life-long and intimate friend of mine he real name be jame b hickok he afterwards become famous as wild bill the scout of the plain -- though why he be so call i never could ascertain -- and from this time forward i shall refer to he by he popular nickname he be ten year my senior -- a tall handsome magnificently build and powerful young fellow who could out-run out-jump and out-fight any man in the train he be generally admit to be the best man physically in the employ of russell major & waddell and of he bravery there be not a doubt general custer in he life on the plain thus speak of wild bill : \* \* \* \* \* among the white scout be number some of the most note of they class the most prominent man among they be ` wild bill ' whose highly vary career be make the subject of a illustrated sketch in one of the popular monthly periodical a few year ago ` wild bill ' be a strange character just the one which a novelist might gloat over he be a plains-man in every sense of the word yet unlike any other of he class in person he be about six foot and one inch in height straight as the straightest of the warrior whose implacable foe he be he have broad shoulder well-formed chest and limb and a face strikingly handsome a sharp clear blue eye which stare you straight in the face when in conversation a finely shaped nose incline to be aquiline a well-turned mouth with lip only partially conceal by a handsome moustache he hair and complexion be those of the perfect blonde the former be worn in uncut ringlet fall carelessly over he powerfully form shoulder add to this figure a costume blend the immaculate neatness of the dandy with the extravagant taste and style of the frontiersman and you have wild bill whether on foot or on horseback he be one of the most perfect type of physical manhood i ever saw of he courage there could be no question it have be bring to the test on too many occasion to admit of a doubt he skill in the use of the pistol and rifle be unerr while he deportment be exactly the opposite of what might be expect from a man of he surroundings it be entirely free from all bluster or bravado he seldom speak himself unless request to do so he conversation strange to say never border either on the vulgar or blasphemous he influence among the frontiersman be unbounded he word be law and many be the personal quarrel and disturbance which he have check among he comrade by he simple announcement that ` this have go far enough ' -- if need be follow by the ominous warning that when persist in or renew the quarreler ` must settle it with I ' wild bill be anything but a quarrelsome man yet no one but he could enumerate the many conflict in which he have be engage and which have almost always result in the death of he adversary i have a personal knowledge of at least half a dozen man whom he have at various time kill one of these be at the time a member of my command other have be severely wound yet he always escape unhurt on the plain every man openly carry he belt with its invariable appendage knife and revolver -- often two of the latter wild bill always carry two handsome ivory-handled revolver of the large size he be never see without they yet in all the many affair of this kind in which wild bill have perform a part and which have come to my knowledge there be not a single instance in which the verdict of twelve fair-minded man would not have be pronounce in he favor \* \* \* \* \* -lrb- illustration : wild bill -rrb- such be the faithful picture of wild bill as draw by general custer who be a close observer and student of personal character and under whom wild bill serve as a scout the circumstance under which i first make he acquaintance and learn to know he well and to appreciate he manly character and kind-heartedness be these one of the teamster in lew simpson 's train be a surly overbearing fellow and take particular delight in bully and tyrannize over I and one day while we be at dinner he ask I to do something for he i do not friendship thus begin continue until he death nothing transpire on the trip to delay or give we any trouble whatever until the train strike the south platte river one day we camp on the same ground you until you can reach fort bridger reply smith and as soon as you cook can get the stuff out of the wagon you can start on foot be the laconic inquiry of simpson yes sir be the equally short reply attempt the recapture of we train when we have travel about two mile we see the smoke arise from we old camp the mormon after take what goods they want and could carry off have set fire to the wagon many of which be load with bacon lard hard-tack and other provision which make a very hot fierce fire and the smoke to roll up in dense cloud some of the wagon be load with ammunition and it be not long before loud explosion follow in rapid succession we wait and witness the burning of the train and then push on to fort bridger arrive at this post we learn that two other train have be capture and destroy in the same way by the mormon this make seventy-five wagon load or 450000 pound of supplies mostly provision which never reach general johnson 's command to which they have be consign chapter vi hard time as it be get very late in the fall we be compel to winter at fort bridger and a long tedious winter it be there be a great many troops there and about four hundred of russell major & waddell 's employee these man be all organize into militia company which be officer by the wagon-master some live in tent other in cabin it be know that we supplies would run short during the winter and so all the man at the post be put on three-quarter ration to begin with before long they be reduce to one-half ration and finally to one-quarter ration we be force to kill we poor worn-out cattle for beef they be actually so poor that we have to prop they up to shoot they down at last we fall back on the mule which be kill and serve up in good style many a poor unsuspecting government mule pass in he chip that winter in order to keep the soldier and bull-whacker from starvation it be really a serious state of affair the wood for the post be obtain from the mountain but have no longer any cattle or mule to transport it the man be oblige to haul it themselves long lariat be tie to the wagon and twenty man man each they be pull to and from the mountain notwithstanding all these hardship the man seem to be contented and to enjoy themselves the winter finally pass away and early in the spring as soon as we could travel the civil employee of the government with the
