square meal once more consist of hard tack bacon coffee and bean i can honestly say that i think it be the best meal i have ever eat at least i relish it more than any other and i think the rest of the party do the same on leave fort laramie simpson be make brigade wagon-master and be put in charge of two large train with about four hundred extra man who be bind for fort leavenworth when we come to ash hollow instead of take the usual trail over to the south platte simpson conclude to follow the north platte down to its junction with the south platte the two train be travel about fifteen mile apart when one morning while simpson be with the rear train he tell he assistant wagon-master george wood and myself to saddle up we mule as he want we to go with he and overtake the head train we start off at about eleven o'clock and have ride about seven mile when -- while we be on a big plateau back of cedar bluff -- we suddenly discover a band of indian come out of the head of a ravine half a mile distant and charge down upon we at full speed i think that we end have come this time sure simpson however take in the situation in a moment and know that it would be impossible to escape by run we played-out mule he adopt a bolder and much better plan he jump from he own mule and tell we to dismount also he then shoot the three animal and as they fall to the ground he cut they throat to stop they kick he then jerk they into the shape of a triangle and order we inside of the barricade all this be but the work of a few moment yet it be not do any too soon for the indian have get within three hundred yard of we and be still advance and utter they demoniacal yell or war-whoops there be forty of the red-skin and only three of we we be each arm with a mississippus yager and two colt 's revolver get ready for they with you gun and when they come within fifty yard aim low blaze away and bring down you man such be the quick command of simpson the word have hardly escape from he mouth when the three yager almost simultaneously belch forth they contents we then seize we revolver and open a lively fire on the enemy at short range which check they advance then we look over we little barricade to ascertain what effect we fire have produce and be much gratify at see three dead indian and one horse lie on the ground only two or three of the indian it seem have fire-arm it must be remember that in those day every indian do not own a needle gun or a winchester rifle as they now do they principal weapon be they bow and arrow see that they could not take we little fortification or drive we from it they circle around we several time shoot they arrow at we one of the arrow strike george wood in the left shoulder inflict only a slight wound however and several lodge in the body of the dead mule otherwise they do we no harm the indian finally gallop off to a safe distance where we bullet could not reach they and seem to be hold a council this be a lucky move for we for it give we a opportunity to reload we gun and pistol and prepare for the next charge of the enemy during the brief cessation of hostility simpson extract the arrow from wood 's shoulder and put a immense quid of tobacco on the wound wood be then ready for business again -lrb- illustration : hold the fort -rrb- the indian do not give we a very long rest for with another desperate charge as if to ride over we they come dash towards the mule barricade we give they a hot reception from we yager and revolver they could not stand or understand the rapidly repeat fire of the revolver and we again check they they circle around we once more and give we a few parting shot as they ride off leave behind they another dead indian and a horse for two hour afterwards they do not seem to be do anything but hold a council we make good use of this time by digging up the ground inside the barricade with we knife and throw the loose earth around and over the mule and we soon have a very respectable fortification we be not trouble any more that day but during the night the cunning rascal try to burn we out by set fire to the prairie the buffalo grass be so short that the fire do not trouble we much but the smoke conceal the indian from we view and they think that they could approach close to we without be see we be aware of this and keep a sharp look-out be prepare all the time to receive they they finally abandon the idea of surprising we next morning bright and early they give we one more grand charge and again we stand they off they then ride away half a mile or so and form a circle around we each man dismount and sit down as if to wait and starve we out they have evidently see the advance train pass on the morning of the previous day and believe that we belong to that outfit and be try to overtake it they have no idea that another train be on its way after we we hope of escape from this unpleasant and perilous situation now depend upon the arrival of the rear train and when we see that the indian be go to besiege we instead of renew they attack we feel rather confident of receive timely assistance we have expect that the train would be along late in the afternoon of the previous day and as the morning wear away we be somewhat anxious and uneasy at its non-arrival at last about ten o'clock we begin to hear in the distance the loud and sharp report of the big bull-whip which be handle with great dexterity by the teamster and crack like rifle shot these be as welcome sound to we as be the note of the bag-pipe to the beseiged garrison at lucknow when the reinforcement be come up and the piper be hear play the campbell be come in a few moment we see the lead or head wagon come slowly over the ridge which have conceal the train from we view and soon the whole outfit make its appearance the indian observe the approach train and assemble in a group they hold a short consultation they then charge upon we once more for the last time and as they turn and dash away over the prairie we send we farewell shot rattle after they the teamster see the indian and hear the shot come rush forward to we assistance but by the time they reach we the red-skin have almost disappear from view the teamster eagerly ask we a hundred question concern we fight admire we fort and praise we pluck simpson 's remarkable presence of mind in plan the defense be the general topic of conversation among all the man when the team come up we obtain some water and bandage with which to dress wood 's wound which have become quite inflamed and painful and we then put he into one of the wagon simpson and myself obtain a remount bid good-bye to we dead mule which have serve we so well and after collect the ornament and other plunder from the dead indian we leave they body and bone to bleach on the prairie the train move on again and we have no other adventure except several exciting buffalo hunt on the south platte near plum creek we arrive at fort leavenworth about the middle of July 1858 when i immediately visit home i find mother in very poor health as she be suffer from asthma my oldest sister martha have during my absence be marry to john crane and be live at leavenworth during the winter at fort bridger i have frequently talk with wild bill about my family and as i have become greatly attach to he i ask he to come and make a visit at we house which he promise to do so one day shortly after we return from fort bridger he accompany I home from leavenworth my mother and sister who have hear so much about he from I be delighted to see he and he spend several week at we place they do everything possible to repay he for he kindness to I ever afterwards when he be at or near leavenworth wild bill come out to we house to see the family whether i be at home or not and he always receive a most cordial reception he mother and sister live in illinoi and he use to call we house he home as he do not have one of he own i have be home only about a month after return from fort bridger when i again start out with another train go this time as assistant wagon-master under buck bomer we go safely through to fort laramie which be we destination and from there we be order to take a load of supplies to a new post call fort wallach which be be establish at cheyenne pass we make this trip and get back to fort laramie about November 1st i then quit the employ of russell major & waddell and join a party of trapper who be send out by the post trader mr ward to trap on the stream of the chugwater and laramie for beaver otter and other fur animal and also to poison wolf for they pelt we be out two month but as the expedition do not prove very profitable and be rather dangerous on account of the indian we abandon the enterprise and come into fort laramie in the latter part of December be anxious to return to the missourus river i join with two other name scott and charley who be also desirous of go east on a visit buy three pony and a pack-mule and we start out together we make rapid progress on we journey and nothing worthy of note happen until one afternoon along the bank of the little blue river we spy a band of indian hunting on the opposite side of the stream three mile away we do not escape they notice and they give we a lively chase for two hour but they could find no good cross and as evening come on we finally get away from they we travel until late in the night when upon discover a low deep ravine which we think would make a comfortable and safe camping-place we stop for a rest in search for a good place to make we bed i find a hole and i call to my companion that i have find a fine place for a nest one of the party be to stand guard while the other sleep scott take the first watch while charley and i make a bed in the hole while clear out the place we feel something rough but as it be dark we could not make out what it be at any rate we conclude that it be bone or stick of wood we think perhaps it might be the bone of some animal which have fall in there and die these bone for such they really prove to be we push one side and then we lay down but charley be a inveterate smoker could not resist the temptation of indulge in a smoke before go to sleep so he sit up and strike a match to light he old pipe we subterranean bed-chamber be thus illuminate for a moment or two i spring to my foot in a instant for a ghastly and horrifying sight be reveal to we eight or ten human skeleton lay scatter upon the ground the light of the match die out but we have see enough to convince we that we be in a large grave into which perhaps some unfortunate emigrant who have be kill by the indian have be throw or perhaps seek refuge there they have be corrale and then kill on the spot if such be the case they have meet the fate of thousand of other whose friend have never hear of they since they leave they eastern home to seek they fortune in the far west however we do not care to investigate this mystery any further but we hustle out of that chamber of death and inform scott of we discovery most of the plains-man be very superstitious and we be no exception to the general rule we surely think that this incident be a evil omen and that we would be kill if we remain there any longer -lrb- illustration : camping in a sepulchre -rrb- let we dig out of here quicker than we can say jack robinson say scott and we begin to dig out at once we saddle we animal and hurriedly push forward through the darkness travel several mile before we again go into camp next morning it be snow fiercely but we proceed as best we could and that night we succeed in reach oak grove ranch which have be build during the summer we here obtain comfortable accommodation and plenty to eat and drink -- especially the latter scott and charley be great lover and consumer of tanglefoot and they soon get gloriously drunk keep it up for three day during which time they gamble with the ranchman who get away with all they money but little they the grass begin grow i become uneasy and discontented and again long for the free and open life of the plain the pike 's peak gold excitement be then at its height and everybody be rush to the new gold digging i catch the gold-fever myself and join a party bind for the new town of aurarium on cherry creek afterwards call denver in honor of the then governor of kansa on arrive at aurarium we push on to the gold stream in the mountain pass up through golden gate and over guy hill and thence on to black hawk we prospect for two month but as none of we know anything about mining we meet with very poor success and we finally conclude that prospect for gold be not we forte we accordingly abandon the enterprise and turn we face eastward once more -lrb- illustration : rafting on the platte -rrb- when we strike the platte river the happy thought of construct a small raft -- which would float we clear to the missourus and thence down to leavenworth -- enter we head and we accordingly carry out the plan upon the completion of the raft we stock it with provision and set sail down the stream it be a light craft and a jolly crew and all be smooth sailing for four or five day when we get near old julesburg we meet with a serious mishap we raft run into a eddy and quick as lightning go to piece throw we all into the stream which be so deep that we have to swim ashore we lose everything we have which greatly discourage we and we thereupon abandon the idea of raft it any farther we then walk over to julesburg which be only a few mile distant this ranch which become a be start the line be be stock with horse and put into good run condition at julesburg i meet mr george chrisman the lead wagon-master of russell major & waddell who have always be a good friend to I he have buy out old jule and be then the owner of julesburg ranch and the agent of the pony express line he hire I at once as a pony express rider but as i be so young he think i would not be able to change of horse i be require to make fifteen mile a hour include the change of horse i be fortunate in get well-broken animal and be so light i easily make my forty-five mile on time on my first trip out and ever afterwards i write to mother and tell she how well i like the exciting life of a pony express rider she reply and beg of I to give it up as it would surely kill I she be right about this as fifteen mile a hour on horseback would in a short time shake any man all to piece and there be but very few if any rider who could stand it for any great length of time nevertheless i stick to it for two month and then upon receive a letter inform I that my mother be very sick i give it up and go back to the old home in salt creek valley chapter vii accident and escape my restless roaming spirit would not allow I to remain at home very long and in November after the recovery of my mother i go up the republican river and its tributary on a trapping expedition in company with dave harrington we outfit consist of one wagon and a yoke of ox for the transportation of provision trap and other necessaries we begin trapping near junction city kansa and then proceed up the republican river to the mouth of prairie dog creek where we find plenty of beaver have see no sign of indian thus far we feel comparatively safe we be catch a large number of beaver and be prosper finely when one of we oxen have become rather poor slip and fall upon the ice dislocate he hip so that we have to shoot he to end he misery this leave we without a team but we care little for that however as we plenty of fresh meat and other provision in the dug-out so that i have no fear of starvation the dugout which we have build immediately after we have determine to remain there all winter be a very cosy hole in the ground cover with pole grass and sod with a fireplace in one end harrington think it would take he twenty day or more to make the round trip but be well provide for -- for this length have happen at sweetwater bridge and with a fresh horse go on and finish the trip without any further adventure -lrb- illustration : attack on stage coach -rrb- about the middle of September the indian there the indian think themselves in comparative safety -- never before have be follow so far into they own country by white man -- have neglect to put out any scout they have no idea that on time slade have take a great fancy to I say : billy i want you to come down to my headquarters and i 'll make you a sort of supernumerary rider and send you out only when it be necessary i accept have plenty of spare time on my hand in this connection i will relate one of my bear-hunting adventure one day when i have nothing else to do i saddle up a extra pony express horse and arm myself with a good rifle and pair of revolver strike out for the foot hill of laramie peak for a bear-hunt ride carelessly along and breathe the cool and brace autumn air which come down from the mountain i feel occur on the overland stage road chapter x questionable proceedings have be away from home nearly a year and have occasionally hear of my mother 's poor health i determine to make she a visit so procure a pass over the road i go to leavenworth arrive there about June 1st 1861 go from there home the civil war have break out and excitement run high in that part of the country my mother of course be a strong union woman and have such great confidence in the government that she believe the war would not last over six month leavenworth at that time be quite a important outfit post for the west and southwest and the fort there be garrison by a large number of troops while in the city one day i meet several of the old as well as the young man who have be member of the free state party all through the kansas trouble and who have like we family lose everything at the hand of the missourian they now think a good opportunity offer to retaliate and get even with they persecutor as they be all consider to be secessionist that they be all secessionist however be not true as all of they do not sympathize with the south but the free state man myself among they take it for grant that as missourus be a slave state the inhabitant must all be secessionist and therefore we enemy a man by the name of chandler propose that we organize a independent company for the purpose of invade missourus and make war on its people on we own responsibility he at once go about it in a very quiet way and succeed in induce twenty-five man to join he in the hazardous enterprise have a longing and party of not more than two or three together and meet at a certain point near westport missourus on a fixed day he instruction be carry out to the letter and we meet at the rendezvous at the appoint -lrb- illustration : nearly every man have two horse -rrb- some of the party boldly take they confiscate horse into leavenworth while other ride they to they home this action may look to the reader like horse-stealing and some people might not hesitate to call it by that name but chandler plausibly maintain that we be only get back we own or the equivalent from the missourian and as the government be wage war against the south it be perfectly square and honest and we have a good right to do it so we do not let we conscience trouble we very much we continue to make similar raid upon the missourian off and on during the summer and occasionally we have run fight with they none of the skirmish however amount to much the government official hearing of we operation put detective upon we track and several of the party be arrest my mother upon learn that i be engage in this business tell I it be neither honorable nor right and she would not for a moment countenance any such proceedings consequently i abandon the jay-hawking enterprise for such it really be about this time the government buy from jone and cartwright several ox-train which be send to rolla missourus all be the watch across the street at nine o'clock and no other man would do it bill then say to tutt that if he attempt anything of the kind he would kill he a challenge to a duel have virtually be give and accept and everybody know that the two man mean business at nine o'clock the next morning tutt start to cross the street wild bill who be stand on the opposite side tell he to stop at that moment tutt who be carry he revolver in he hand fire at bill but miss he bill quickly pull out he revolver and return the fire hit tutt squarely in the forehead and kill he instantly quite a number of tutt 's friend be stand in the vicinity have assemble to witness the duel and bill as soon as tutt fall to the ground turn to they and ask if any one of they want to take it up for tutt if so he would accommodate any of they then and there but none of they care to stand in front of wild bill to be shoot at by he nothing of course be ever do to bill for the killing of tutt chapter xi a soldier in the fall of 1861 i make a trip to fort larned kansa carry military dispatch and in the winter i accompany george long through the country and assist he in buy horse for the government the next spring 1862 a expedition against the indian be organize consist of a volunteer regiment the ninth kansa under colonel clark this expedition which i have join in the capacity of guide and scout proceed to the kiowa and comanche country on the arkansa river along which stream we scout all summer between fort lyon and fort larn on the old santa fe trail we have several engagement with the indian but they be of no great importance in the winter of 1862 i become one of the red legged scout -- a company of scout command by captain tuff among its member be some of the most note kansa ranger such as red clark the st clair brother jack harvey a old pony express-rider name johnny fry and many other well know frontiersman we field of operation be confine mostly to the arkansa country and southwestern missourus we have many a lively skirmish with the bushwhacker and younger brother and when we be not hunting they we be generally employ in carry dispatch between fort dodge gibson leavenworth and other post whenever we be in leavenworth we have a very festive time we usually attend all the ball in full force and run thing to suit ourselves thus i pass the winter of 1862 and the spring of 1863 subsequently i engage to conduct a small train to denver for some merchant and on reach that place in September i receive a letter state that my mother be not expect to live i hasten home and find she dangerously ill she grow gradually worse and at last on the 22d of November 1863 she die thus pass away a loving and affectionate mother and a noble brave good and loyal woman that i love she above all other person no one who have read these reminiscence can for a moment doubt previous to this say event my sister julium have be marry to a gentleman name ja goodman and they now come to reside at we house and take charge of the child as my mother have desire that they should not be separate mr goodman become the guardian of the minor child i soon leave the home now render gloomy by the absence of she whom i have so tenderly love and go to leavenworth i enter upon a dissolute and reckless life -- to my shame be it say -- and associate with gambler drunkard and bad character generally i continue my dissipation about two month and be become a very hard case about this time the seventh kansa regiment know as jennison 's jay-hawker return from the war and re-enlist and re-organize as veteran among they i meet quite a number of my old comrade and neighbor who try to induce I to enlist and go south with they i have no idea of do anything of the kind but one day after have be under the influence of bad whisky i awake to find myself a soldier in the seventh kansa i do not remember how or when i have enlist but i see i be in for it and that it would not do for I to endeavor to back out in the spring of 1864 the regiment be order to tennessee and we get into memphi just about the time that general sturgi be so badly whip by general forrest general a j smith re-organize the army to operate against forrest and after march to tupalo mississippus we have a engagement with he and defeat he this kind of fighting be all new to I be entirely different from any in which i have ever before engage i soon become a non-commissioned officer and be put on detach service as a scout after skirmish around the country with the rest of the army for some little time we regiment return to memphi but be immediately order to cape girardeau in missourus as a confederate force under general price be then raiding that state the command of which my regiment be a part hurry to the front to intercept price and we first fight with he occur at pilot knob from that time for nearly six week we fight or skirmish every day i be still act as a scout when one day i ride ahead of the command some considerable distance to pick up all possible information concern price 's movement i be dress in gray clothes or missourus jeans and on ride up to a farm-house and enter i see a man also dress in gray costume sit at a table eating bread and milk he look up as i enter and startle I by say : you little rascal what be you do in those ` secesh ' clothes judge of my surprise when i recognize in the stranger my old friend and partner wild bill disguise as a confederate officer i ask you the same question sir say i without the least hesitation hush sit down and have some bread and milk and we 'll talk it all over afterwards say he i accept the invitation and partook of the refreshment wild bill pay the woman of the house and we go out to the gate where my horse be stand billy my boy say he i be mighty glad to see you i have not see or hear of you since we get bust on that st loui ' horse-race what be you do out here i ask i be a scout under general mcniel for the last few day i have be with general marmaduke 's division of price 's army in disguise as a southern officer from texa as you see I now say he that be exactly the kind of business that i be out on to-day say i and i want to get some information concern price 's movement i 'll give you all that i have and he then go on and tell I all that he know regard price 's intention and the number and condition of he man he then ask about my mother and when he learn that she be dead he be greatly surprised and grieve he think a great deal of she for she have treat he almost as one of she own child he finally take out a package which he have conceal about he person and hand it to I he say : here be some letter which i want you to give to general mcniel all right say i as i take they but where will i meet you again never mind that he reply i be get so much valuable information that i propose to stay a little while longer in this disguise thereupon we shake hand and part it be not necessary to say much concern price 's raid in general as that event be a matter of recorded history i be only relate the incident in which i be personally interested either as one of the actor or as a observer another interesting and i may say exciting episode happen to I a day or two after my unexpected meeting with wild bill i be ride with the advance guard of we army and wish a drink of water i stop at a farmhouse there be no man about the premise and no one except a very fine and intellectual look lady and she two daughter they seem to be almost frighten to death at see I -- a yank -- appear before they i quiet they fear somewhat and the mother then ask I how far back the army be when i tell she it would be along shortly she express she fear that they would take everything on the premise they set I out a lunch and treat I rather kindly so that i really begin to sympathize with they for i know that the soldier would ransack they house and confiscate everything they could lay they hand on at last i resolve to do what i could to protect they after the general and the staff officer have pass by i take it upon myself to be a sentry over the house when the command come along some of the man rush up with the intention of enter the place and carry off all the desirable plunder possible and then tear and break everything to piece as they usually do along the line of march halt i shout i have be place here by the commanding officer as a guard over this house and no man must enter it this stop the first squad and see that my plan be a success i remain at my post during the passage of the entire command and keep out all intruder it seem as if the lady could not thank I sufficiently for the protection i have afford they they be perfectly aware of the fact that i have act without order and entirely on my own responsibility and therefore they feel the more grateful they urgently invite I to remain a little while longer and partake of a excellent dinner which they say they be prepare for I i be pretty hungry about that time as we ration have be rather slim of late and a good dinner be a temptation i could not withstand especially as it be to be serve up by such elegant lady while i be eat the meal i be most agreeably entertain by the young lady and before i have finish it the last of the rear-guard must have be at least two mile from the house suddenly three man enter the room and i look up and see three double-barreled shot-gun level straight at I before i could speak however the mother and she daughter spring between the man and I father boy lower you gun you must not shoot this man and hair of you head for the world but it be best that you stay here no longer as you command be some distance from here now and you might be cut off by bushwhacker before reach it bid they all good-bye and with many thanks from the mother and daughter i mount my horse and soon overtake the column happy in the thought that i have do a good deed and with no regret that i have save from pillage and destruction the home and property of a confederate and he family we command keep crowd against price and he army until they be push into the vicinity of kansas city where they further advance be check spend two week there in have a jolly good time as some people would express it chapter xii a wedding it be during the winter of 1864-65 while i be on detach service at military headquarters at st loui in obtain employment during the winter of 1866-67 i scout between fort ellsworth and fort fletcher in the spring of 1867 i be at fort fletcher when general custer come out to go on a indian expedition with general hancock i remain at this post until it be drown out by the heavy flood of big creek on which it be located the water rise about the fortification and render the place unfit for occupancy so the government abandon the fort and move the troops and supplies to a new post -- which have be name fort hay -- located further west on the south fork of big creek it be while scout in the larn a distance of sixty-five mile across the country i be order by the commanding officer to guide general custer to he desire destination and i soon receive word from the general that he would start out in the morning with the intention of make the trip in one day early in the morning after a good night 's rest i be on hand mount on my large mouse-colored mule -- a animal of great endurance -- and ready for the journey when the general saw I he say : cody i want to travel fast and go through as quickly as possible and i do not think that mule of yours be fast enough to suit I general never river and strike the sand-hill i begin let my mule out a little and put the persuader to he he be soon out-traveling the horse and by the time we have make about half the distance to fort larned i occasionally have to wait for the general or some of he party as they horse be begin to show sign of fatigue general how about this mule anyhow i ask at last cody you have a better vehicle than i think you have be he reply from that time on to fort larned i have no trouble in keep ahead of the party we ride into the fort at four o'clock in the afternoon with about half the escort only the rest custer whom i always admire as a man and as a officer -lrb- illustration : general custer -rrb- a few day after my return to fort hay the indian make a raid on the kansas pacific railroad kill five or company and one mountain howitzer to go in pursuit of the red-skin and i be send along with the expedition as scout and guide on the second day out we suddenly discover on the opposite side of the saline river about a mile distant a large body of indian who be charge down upon we major arm place the cannon on a little knoll limber it up and leave twenty man to guard it and then with the rest of the command he cross the river to meet the indian just as he have get the man over the stream we hear a terrific yell and shout in we rear and look back to the knoll where the cannon have be station we see the negro who have be leave there to guard the gun fly towards we be pursue by about one hundred indian while another large party of the latter be dance around the capture cannon as if they have get hold of a elephant and do not know what to do with it major arm turn he command back and drive the indian from the gun the troops then dismount and take position there quite a severe fight large party the color troops who have be brag all the way that if they could only see some indian dey would blow 'em off de farm -- which be a favorite expression of theirs -- be now sing a different tune every time the indian would make a charge at we the darkey would cry out : heah dey cum dey must be ten thousand ob 'em de whole country be alive wid 'em massa bill do you tink we be eber agoin ' to get out o ' heah and many other similar expression major arm who be wound and lie under the cannon -- which by the way have become useless -- call I up and ask if i think there be any show of get back to the fort i reply that there be order be accordingly give by major arm for a retreat the cannon be leave behind during the movement several of we man be kill but as night come and dense darkness prevail we succeed in make good headway and get into fort hay just at daylight next morning in a very played-out condition during we absence the cholera have break out at the post and five or six man be die daily it be difficult to tell which be the greater danger -- fight indian on the prairie or face the cholera in camp but the former be decidedly the more invite chapter xiii a millionaire soon after return to fort hay i be send with dispatch to fort harker after deliver the message i visit the town of ellsworth about three mile west of fort harker and there i meet a man name william rise a contractor on the kansas pacific railroad who have a contract for grading near fort hay he have have he stock steal by the indian and have come to ellsworth to buy more during the course of we conversation mr rise incidentally remark that he have some idea of lay out a town on the west side of big creek about one mile from the fort where the railroad be to cross he ask my opinion of the contemplated enterprise and i tell he that i think it be a big thing he then propose take I as a partner in the scheme and suggest that after we get the town lay out and throw open to the public we should establish a store and saloon there think it would be a grand thing to be half-owner of a town i at once accept he proposition we buy a stock of such article as be usually find in a frontier store and transport they to the place on big creek where we be to find we town we hire a railroad engineer to survey the site and stake it off into lot and we give the new town the ancient be on a bright summer morning that we sit on a pine box in front of we crib moodily view the demolition of the last building three day before we have consider ourselves millionaire on that morning we rome entirely mr rise facetiously remark that he feel like the last rose of summer with all he lovely companion fade and go and _ he _ leave bloom alone i tell he i be still there staunch and true but he reply that that do not help the matter much thus end the brief history of the rise decline and fall of modern rome it have become evident to I that there be very little hope of rome ever regain its former splendor and prosperity i send my wife and daughter arta -- who have be bear at leavenworth in the latter part of December 1866 -- to st loui on a visit they have be live with I for some little and run through the site of rome notwithstanding we have be desert we have some small hope that they would not be able to get water at the new town and that the people would all soon move back to rome be then about three-quarter of a mile distant and we stop and wave we hat at they and fire some shot at long range there be thirteen in the party and as they be get pretty close to we we strike out for hay they come on in pursuit and send several scatter shot after we but we easily leave they behind they finally turn and ride off towards the saline river the doctor think this glorious sport and want to organize a party to go in pursuit of they but i induce he to give up this idea although he do so rather reluctantly the doctor soon become quite a expert hunter and before he have remain on the prairie a year there be but few man in the country who could kill more buffalo on a hunt than he be aware that rise and myself feel rather downheart over we desert village the doctor one day say supper i have no saddle as mine have be leave at the camp a mile distant so take the harness from brigham i mount he bareback and start out after the game be arm with my celebrated buffalo-killer this connection i will here give a brief history of that memorable event -lrb- illustration : general phil sheridan -rrb- the indian have become quite troublesome and general sheridan have select take the field and on the morning of the 29th of August 1868 they ride out of fort hay to meet the indian lieutenant fh beecher of the third infantry nephew of henry ward beecher be second in command would find they and give they a fight early next morning September 19th the cry of indian startle the command every man jump for he horse a half-dozen red-skin yell and whoop and make a hideous racket and firing they gun ride up and attempt to stampede the horse several of which together with the four pack-mule be so frightened that they break loose and get away the indian then ride off follow by a few shot in a minute afterwards hundred of indian warrior -- it be estimate that there be nearly one thousand -- come gallop down upon the command from every quarter completely hem they in act under the order of general forsyth the man retreat to a small island tie they horse in a circle to the bush and then throw themselves upon the ground they begin the defense by firing at the approach enemy who come pretty close and give they a rake fire the besiege scout at the first opportunity throw up a small breastwork with they knife the firing however continue back and forth and early in the fight forsyth be twice seriously wound -- once in the right thigh and once in the left leg dr mower be also wound in the head and soon die two other man have be kill and several wound all the horse of the command be kill by nine o'clock in the morning shortly afterwards over three hundred dog-soldier indian command by old roman nose charge down upon the little band of hero give they volley after volley but finally the scout at a favorable opportunity return they fire with tell effect roman nose and medicine man be kill and fall from they horse when within less than one rod of the scout who thereupon send up a triumphant shout the charge brave now weaken and in a few moment they be drive back it be a brilliant charge and be most nobly and bravely repulse the scout have again suffer severely have several man wound among the number be lieutenant beecher who die that night the indian too have have quite a number kill several of whom have fall close to the earthwork the dismounted indian warrior still continue firing but as the scout have throw up they intrenchment sufficiently to protect themselves by closely hug the ground little or no damage be do a second charge be make by the mount indian about two o'clock in the afternoon and they be again repulse with a severe loss darkness finally come on and then ensue a cessation of hostility two of the scout have be kill four fatally wound and fourteen other be wound more or less severely there be just twenty-eight able-bodied man leave out of the fifty the supplies have run out and as dr mower have be mortally wound and the medical store capture the wound man could not be properly care for although they be entirely surround and one hundred and ten mile from the nearest post the man do not despair they have a abundance of ammunition plenty of water under ground only a short distance and for food they have they horse and mule at night two of the scout tradeau and stillwell steal through the line of the indian and start swiftly for fort wallace to obtain relief it be a dangerous undertaking but they be brave and experience scout stillwell be only nineteen or twenty year old but he be in every sense of the word a thoroughbred frontiersman during the night the besiege scout throw up they breastwork considerably higher and pile the dead animal on top they dig down to water and also store away a lot of horse and mule meat in the sand to keep it fresh as long as possible the indian renew they firing next morning and keep it up all day do but little injury however as the scout be now well entrenched but many a indian be send to he happy hunting ground -lrb- illustration : battle on the arickaree -rrb- night come again and the prospects be indeed gloomy a attempt be make by two more of the scout to creep through the indian line but they be detect by the enemy and have to return to they comrade the next morning the indian renew hostility as usual they woman and child begin to disappear about noon and then the indian try to draw the scout out by display a white flag for a truce they appear to want to have a talk with general forsyth but as they treachery be well-known the scout do not fall into this trap the indian have apparently become tired of fight especially as they find that they have a most stubborn foe to deal with night once more throw its mantle over the scene and under the cover of the darkness donovan and plyley two of the best scout stealthily make they way out of the camp and start for fort wallace with a dispatch from general forsyth who give a brief summary of the situation and state that if necessary he could hold out for six day longer when the day dawn again only a small number of warrior could be see and they probably remain to watch the scout and keep they corrale the uninjured man attend to the wound as well as they could under the adverse circumstance but from want of proper treatment evidence of gangrene appear in some of the wound on the sixth day the mule and horse meat become totally unfit for use but they have nothing else to eat and have to eat it or starve under these try circumstance the general tell the man that any who wish to go might do so and take they chance but they all resolve to remain and die together if need be relief come at last tradeau and stillwell have safely reach fort wallace and on the morning of the 25th of September colonel carpenter and a detachment of cavalry arrive with supplies this assistance to the besiege and starve scout come like a vessel to ship-wrecked man drift and starve on a raft in mid-ocean it be with the survivor of this terrible fight that i spend the few day at hay city prior to the arrival of the fifth cavalry chapter xviii scout on the third day of October the fifth cavalry arrive at fort hay and i at once begin make the acquaintance of the different officer of the regiment i be introduce by general sheridan to colonel william royal who be in command of the regiment he be a gallant officer and a agreeable and pleasant gentleman he be now station at omaha as inspector general in the department of the platte i also become acquaint with major wh brown major walker captain sweetman quartermaster em hay and in fact all the officer of the regiment general sheridan be anxious to punish the indian who have lately fight general forsyth do not give the regiment much of a rest and accordingly on the 5th of October it begin its march for the beaver creek country the first night we camp on the south fork of big creek four mile west of hay city by this time i have become pretty well acquaint with major brown and captain sweetman who invite I to mess with they on this expedition and a jolly mess we have there be other scout in the command besides myself and i particularly remember tom renahan hank field and a character call nosey on account of he long nose on the morning of the 6th we pull out to the north and during the day i be very favorably strike with the appearance of the regiment it be a beautiful command and when string out on the prairie with a train of seventy-five six-mule wagon ambulance and pack mule i feel very proud of my position as guide and chief of scout of such a warlike expedition just as we be about to go into camp on the saline river that night we run on to a band of about fifteen indian who see we dash across the creek follow by some bullet which we send after they but as the small band prove to be a scout party we pursue they only a mile or two when we attention be direct to a herd of buffalo -- they be very plenty -- and we succeed in kill ten or fifteen for the command the next day we march thirty mile and late in the afternoon we go into camp on the south fork of the solomon at this encampment colonel royal ask I to go out and kill some buffalo for the boy all right colonel send along a wagon or two to bring in the meat i say i be not in the habit of send out my wagon until i know that there be something to be haul in kill you buffalo first and then i 'll send out the wagon be the colonel 's reply i say no more but go out on a hunt and after a short absence return and ask the colonel to send he wagon over the hill for the half dozen buffalo i have kill the follow afternoon he again request I to go out and get some fresh buffalo meat i do not ask he for any wagon this time but ride out some distance and come up with a small herd i manage to get seven of they head straight for the encampment and instead of shoot they just then i run they at full speed right into the camp and then kill they all one after the other in rapid succession colonel royal witness the whole proceeding which puzzle he somewhat as he could see no reason why i have not kill they on the prairie he come up rather angrily and demand a explanation i can not allow any such business as this cody say he what do you mean by it i do not care about ask for any wagon this time colonel so i think i would make the buffalo furnish they own transportation be my reply the colonel see the point in a moment and have no more to say on the subject -lrb- illustration : bring meat into camp -rrb- no indian have be see in the vicinity during the day and colonel royal have carefully post he picket suppose everything be serene for the night but before morning we be rouse from we slumber by hear shot fire and immediately afterwards one of the mount picket come gallop into camp say that there be indian close at hand the company all fall into line and be soon prepared and anxious to give the red-skins battle that major brown and i be out on a lark and therefore there be not much say about we exploit halt with a grand flourish in front of he tent major brown jump out in he most gallant style and politely from the dépôt next morning at a early hour the command start out on a hunt for indian general carr have a pretty good idea where he would be most likely to find they direct I to guide he by the nearest route to elephant rock on beaver creek upon arrive at the south fork of the beaver on the second day 's march we discover a large fresh indian trail which we hurriedly follow for a distance of to give we battle they set fire to the prairie grass in front of we and on all side in order to delay we as much as possible we keep up a run fight for the remainder of the afternoon and the indian repeatedly attempt to lead we off the track of they fly village but they trail be easily follow as they be continually drop tepee pole camp kettle robe fur and all heavy article belong to they they be hard and give they such a scare that they would leave the republican country and go north across the union pacific railroad most of the indian as he have predict do cross the platte river near illustration : a hard crowd -rrb- chapter xix a tough time general carr soon receive order from general sheridan that he be to make a winter 's campaign in the canadian river country and that we be to proceed to fort lyon on the arkansa river in colorado and there fit out for the expedition leave fort wallace in November 1868 we arrive at fort lyon in the latter part of the month and outfit for the come expedition general penrose have leave this post three week previously with a command of some three hundred man he have take no wagon with he and he supply train be compose only of pack mule general carr be order to follow with supplies on he trail and overtake he as soon as possible i be particularly anxious to catch up with penrose 's command as my old friend wild bill be among he scout we follow the trail very easily for the first three day and then we be catch in freeze-out canyon by a fearful snow storm which compel we to go into camp for a day the ground now be cover with snow we find that it would be almost impossible to follow penrose 's trail any further especially as he have leave no sign to indicate the direction he be go general carr send for I and say that as it be very penrose or where he have camp at any time -lrb- illustration : camping in the snow -rrb- accompany by four man i start out in the blinding snow storm take a southerly direction we ride twenty-four i hastily dress and accompany captain ezekiel to fort wallace arrive there at two o'clock in the morning bill i be really sorry say captain ezekiel as we alight but i have order to place you in the guard-house and i must perform my duty very well captain i do not blame you a bit say i and into the guard-house i go as a prisoner for the first and only time in my life the sergeant of the -- guard who be a old friend of mine belong to captain graham 's company which be station there at the time -- do not put I into a cell but kindly allow I to stay in he room and occupy he bed and in a few minute i be snore away as if nothing unusual have occur shortly after _ reveille _ captain graham call to see I he think it be a shame for I to be in the guard-house and say that he would interview general bankhead in my behalf as soon as he get up the captain have a nice breakfast prepare for I and then depart at guard-mount i be not send for contrary to my expectation and thereupon i have word convey to captain graham who be officer of the day that i want to see general bankhead the captain inform I that the general absolutely refuse to hold any conversation whatever with I at this time there be no telegraph line between fort wallace and fort lyon and therefore it be impossible for I to telegraph to general carr and i determine to send a dispatch direct to general sheridan i accordingly write out a long telegram inform he of my difficulty and have it take to the telegraph office for transmission but the operator instead of send it at once as he should have do show it to general bankhead who tear it up and instruct the operator not to pay any attention to what i might say as he be run that post think it very strange that i receive no answer during the day i go to the telegraph office accompany by a guard and learn from the operator what he have do see here my young friend say i this be a public telegraph line and i want my telegram send or there 'll be trouble i re-wrote my dispatch and hand it to he accompany with the money to pay for the transmission say as i do so : young man i wish that telegram send direct to chicago you know it be you duty to send it and it must go he know very well that he be compel to transmit the message but before do so he call on general bankhead and inform he of what i have say and tell he that he would certainly have to send it for if he do not he might lose he position the general see that the telegram would have to go summon I to he headquarters and the first thing he say after i get into he presence be : if i let you go sir will you leave the post at once and not bother my agent at sheridan again no sir i reply i 'll do nothing of the kind i 'll remain in the guard-house until i receive a answer from general sheridan if i give you the horse and mule will you proceed at once to fort lyon no sir i have some bill to settle at sheridan and some other business to transact reply i well sir will you at least agree not to interfere any further with the quartermaster 's agent at sheridan i shall not bother he any more sir as i have have all i want from he be my answer general bankhead thereupon send for captain laufer and order he to turn the horse and mule over to I in a few minute more i be on my way to sheridan and after settle my business there i proceed to fort lyon arrive two day afterwards i related my adventure to general carr major brown and other officer who be greatly amuse thereby i be glad you have come bill say general carr as i have be want you for the last two week while we have be at this post several valuable animal as well as a large number of government horse and mule have be steal and we think that the thief be still in the vicinity of the fort but as yet we have be unable to discover they rendezvous i have have a party out for the last few day in the neighborhood of old fort lyon and they have find fresh track down there and seem to think that the stock be conceal somewhere in the timber along the arkansa river bill green one of the scout who have just come up from there can perhaps tell you something more about the matter green who have be summon say that he have discover fresh trail before strike the heavy timber opposite old fort lyon but that in the tall grass he could not follow they he have mark the place where he have last see fresh mule track so that he could find it again now cody you be just the person we want say the general very well i 'll get a fresh mount and to-morrow i 'll go down and see what i can discover say i you have better take two man besides green and a pack mule with eight or ten day ' ration suggest the general so that if you find the trail you can follow it up as i be very anxious to get back this steal property the scoundrel have take one of my private horse and also lieutenant forbush 's favorite little black race mule next morning i start out after the horse-thief be accompany by green jack farley and another scout the mule track mark by green be easily find and with very little difficulty i follow it for about two mile into the timber and come upon a place where as i could plainly see from numerous sign quite a number of head of stock have be tie among the tree and keep for several day this be evidently the spot where the thief have be hide they steal stock until they have accumulate quite a herd from this point it be difficult to trail they as they have take the steal animal out of the timber one by one and in different direction thus show that they be expert at the business and experience frontiersman for no indian could have exhibit more cunning in cover up a trail than do they i abandon the idea of follow they trail in this immediate locality so call my man together i tell they that we would ride out for about five mile and make a complete circuit about the place and in this way we would certainly find the trail on which they have move out while make the circuit we discover the track of twelve animal -- four mule and eight horse -- in the edge of some sand-hill and from this point we have no trouble in trail they down the arkansa river which they have cross at sand creek and then have go up the latter stream in the direction of denver to which place they be undoubtedly bind when near denver they trail become so obscure that we at last lose it but by inquire of the settler along the road which they have take we occasionally hear of they when within four mile of denver -- this be on a Thursday -- we learn that the horse-thief have pass there two day before i come to the conclusion they would attempt to dispose of the animal in denver and be aware that Saturday be the great auction day there i think it best to remain where we be at a hotel and not go into the city until that day it certainly would not have be advisable for I to have go into denver meantime -- because i be well-known there and if the thief have learn of my presence in the city they would at once have suspect my business early Saturday morning we ride into town and stable we horse at the elephant corral i secure a room from ed chase overlook the corral and then take up my post of observation i do not have long to wait for a man whom i readily recognize as one of we old packer ride into the corral mount upon lieutenant forbush 's racing mule and lead another government mule which i also identify it have be recently brand and over the we be a plain db i wait for the man 's companion to put in a appearance but he do not come and my conclusion be that he be secrete outside of the city with the rest of the animal presently the black mule belong to forbush be put up at auction now think i be the time to do my work so walk through the crowd who be bidding for the mule i approach the man who have offer he for sale he recognize I and endeavor to escape but i seize he by the shoulder say : i guess my friend that you 'll have to go with I if you make any resistance i 'll shoot you on the spot he be arm with a pair of pistol which i take away from he then inform the auctioneer that i be a united state detective and show he -- as well as a inquisitive officer -- my commission as such i tell he to stop the sale as the mule be steal property and that i have arrest the thief whose name be williams farley and green who be near at hand now come forward and together we take the prisoner and the mule three mile down the platte river there in a thick bunch of timber we all dismount and make preparation to hang william from a limb if he do not tell we where he partner be at first he deny know anything about any partner or any other stock but when he see that we be in earnest and would hang he at the end of the give time -- five minute -- unless he squeal he tell we that he pal be at a unoccupied house three mile further down the river we immediately proceed to the spot indicate and as we come within sight of the house we see we stock grazing near by just as we ride up to the door another one of we old packer whom i recognize as bill bevin step to the front and i cover he instantly with my rifle before he could draw he revolver i order he to throw up he hand and he obey the command green then disarm he and bring he out we look through the house and find they saddle pack-saddle blanket overcoat lariat and two henry rifle which we take possession of the horse and mule we tie in a bunch and with the whole outfit we return to denver where we lodge william and bevin in jail in charge of my friend sheriff edward cook the next day we take they out and tie each one on a mule we strike out on we return trip to fort lyon at the hotel outside the city where we have stop on Thursday and Friday we be join by we man with the pack-mule that night we camp on cherry creek seventeen mile from denver the weather -- it be in April -- be cold and stormy but we find a warm and cosy camping place in a bend of the creek we make we bed in a row with we foot towards the fire the prisoner so far have appear very docile and have make no attempt to escape and therefore i do not think it necessary to hobble they we make they sleep on the inside and it be so arrange that some one of we should be on guard all the time at about one o'clock in the night it begin snow while i be watch shortly before three o'clock jack farley who be then on guard and sit on the foot of the bed with he back to the prisoner be kick clear into the fire by william and the next moment bevin who have get hold of he shoe -- which i have think be out of he reach -- spring up and jump over the fire and start on a run i send a shot after he as soon as i awake sufficiently to comprehend what be take place william attempt to follow he and as he do so i whirl around and knock he down with my revolver farley by this time have gather himself out of the fire and green have start after bevin firing at he on the run but the prisoner make he escape into the brush in he flight unfortunately for he and luckily for we he drop one of he shoe leave william in the charge of farley and long doc as we call the man with the pack-mule green and myself strike out after bevin as fast as possible we hear he break through the brush but know that it would be useless to follow he on foot we go back to the camp and saddle up two of the fastest horse and at daylight we strike out on he trail which be plainly visible in the snow he have get a hour and a half the start of we he track lead we in the direction of the mountain and the south platte river and as the country through which he be pass be cover with prickly pear we know that he could not escape step on they with he one bare foot and hence we be likely to overtake he in a short time we could see however from the long jump that he be take that he be make excellent time but we frequently notice after we have go some distance that the prickly pear and stone along he route be cut he bare foot as nearly every track of it be spot with blood we have run we horse some twelve mile when we see bevin cross a ridge about two mile ahead urge we horse up to they utmost speed we reach the ridge just as he be descend the divide towards the south platte which stream be very deep and swift at this point it become evident that if he should cross it ahead of we he would have a good chance of make he escape so push we steed as fast as possible we rapidly gain on he and when within a hundred yard of he i cry to he to halt or i would shoot know i be a good shot he stop and coolly sit down wait till we come up bevin you have give we a good run say i yes say he and if i have have fifteen minute more of a start and get across the platte i would have laugh at the idea of you ever catch I bevin 's run be the most remarkable feat of the kind ever know either of a white man or a indian a man who could run bare-footed in the snow eighteen mile through a prickly pear patch be certainly a tough one and that be the kind of a person bill bevin be upon look at he bleed foot i really feel sorry for he he ask I for my knife and i give he my sharp-pointed bowie with which he dig the prickly pear briar out of he foot i consider he as game a man as i have ever meet bevin i have get to take you back say i but as you can not walk with that foot you can ride my horse and i 'll foot it we accordingly start back for we camp with bevin on my horse which be lead either by green or myself as we alternately ride the other horse we keep a close watch on bevin for we have ample proof that he need watch he wounded foot must have pained he terribly but not a word of complaint escape he on arrive at the camp we find william bind as we have leave he and he seem sorry that we have capture bevin -lrb- illustration : the recapture of bevin -rrb- after breakfast we resume we journey and nothing worth of note again occur until we reach the arkansa river where we find a vacant cabin and at once take possession of it for the night there be no likelihood of bevin again try to escape for he foot have swollen to a enormous size and be useless believe that william could not escape from the cabin we unbound he we then go to sleep leave long doc on guard the cabin be comfortably warm and well light by the fire it be a dark stormy night -- so dark that you could hardly see you hand before you at about ten o'clock williams ask long doc to allow he to step to the door for a moment long doc who have he revolver in he hand do not think it necessary to wake we up and believe that he could take care of the prisoner he grant he revolver he have dodge around the house doc jump after he and fire just as he turn a corner the report bring we all to we foot and in a instant we know what have happen i at once cover bevin with my revolver but as i see that he could hardly stir and be make no demonstration i lower the weapon just then doc come in swearing a blue streak and announce that william have escape there be nothing for see or hear of william we finally get back to fort lyon with bevin and general carr to whom i immediately report compliment we highly on the success of we trip notwithstanding we have lose one prisoner the next day we take bevin to bogg ' ranch on picket wire creek and there turn he over to the civil authority who put he in a log jail to await he trial he never be try however for he soon make he escape as i expect he would do i hear no more of he until 1872 when i learn that he be skirmish around on laramie plain at he old trick he send word by the gentleman from whom i gain this information that if he ever meet I again he would kill I on sight he finally be arrest and convict for robbery and be confine in the prison at laramie city again he make he escape and soon afterwards he organize a desperate gang of outlaw who infested the country north of the union pacific railroad and when the stage begin to run between cheyenne and deadwood in the black hill they rob the coach and passenger frequently make large haul of plunder they keep this up for some time till finally most of the gang be catch try convict and send to the penitentiary for a number of year bill bevin and nearly all of he gang be now confine in the nebraska state prison to which they be transfer from wyome -lrb- illustration : rob a stage coach -rrb- chapter xxi a military expedition a day or two after my return to fort lyon the fifth cavalry be order to the department of the platte and take up they line of march for fort mcpherson nebraska we lay over one day at fort wallace to get supplies and while there i have occasion to pass general bankhead 's headquarters he orderly call to I and say the general wish to see I as i enter the general 's office he extend he hand and say : i hope you have arrangement and from that time forward we trade we liquid for they solid when the rest of the officer hear of what brown and i have do they all send we invitation to dine with they at any time we return the compliment by invite they to drink with we whenever they be dry although i would not advise anybody to follow we example yet it be a fact that we get more provision for we whiskey than the same money which we pay for the liquor would have buy so after all it prove a very profitable investment on reach the north fork of the beaver and ride down the valley towards the stream i suddenly discover a large fresh indian trail on examination i find it to be scatter all over the valley on both side of the creek as if a very large village have recently pass down that way judge from the size of the trail i think there could not be less than four hundred lodge or between twenty-five hundred and three thousand warrior woman and child in the band i galloped hack to the command distant about three mile and report the news to general carr who halt the regiment and after consult a few minute order I to select a ravine or as low ground as possible so that he could keep the troops out of the indian be travel i be soon convince by the many camp they have make that they be travel slowly and hunting as they journey we go down the beaver on this scout about twelve mile keep we horse well the pawnee indian unlike regular soldier have not wait to receive order from they officer but have jump on they pony without bridle or saddle and place rope in they mouth have dash off in the could ride i give he the name of buckskin joe and he prove to be a second brigham that horse i ride on and off during the summer of 1869 1870 1871 and 1872 and he be the horse that the grand duke alexi ride on he buffalo hunt in the winter of 1872 after i have leave fort mcpherson buckskin joe be condemn and sell at public sale and be buy by dave perry at north platte who in 1877 present he to I and i still own he he be now at my ranch on the dismal river stone blind but i shall keep he until he die the command scout several day up the beaver and prairie dog river occasionally have run I but while at this camp i gain they respect and admiration by show they how i kill buffalo although the pawnee be excellent buffalo killer for indian i have never see one of they who could kill more and some of the officer and see they make a surround twenty of the pawnee circle a herd and succeed in kill only thirty-two while they be cut up the animal another herd appear in sight the indian be prepare to surround it when i ask major north to keep they back and let I show they what i could do he accordingly inform the indian of my wish and they readily consent to let I have the opportunity i have learn that buckskin joe be a excellent buffalo horse and feel confident that i would astonish the native gallop in among the buffalo i certainly do so by kill thirty-six in less than a half-mile run at nearly every shot i kill a buffalo string the dead animal out on the prairie not over fifty foot apart this manner of killing be greatly admire by the indian who call I a big chief and from that time on i stand high in they estimation chapter xxii a desperate fight on leave camp the command take a westward course up the republican and major north with two company of he pawnee and two or three company of cavalry under the command of colonel royal make a scout to the north of the river shortly after we have go into camp on the black tail deer fork we observe a band of indian come over the prairie at full gallop singing and yell and wave they lance and long pole at first we suppose they to be sioux and all be excitement for a few moment we notice however that we pawnee indian make no hostile demonstration or preparation towards go out to fight they but begin swing and yell themselves captain lute north step up to general carr and say : general those be we man who be come and they have have a fight that be the way they act when they come back from a battle and have take any scalp the pawnee come into camp on the run captain north call to one of they -- a sergeant -- soon find out that they have run across a party of sioux who be follow a large indian trail these indian have evidently be in a fight for two or three of they have be wound and they be convey the injured person on _ travoi _ the pawnee have jump they and have kill three or four more of they next morning the command at a early hour start out to take up this indian trail which they follow for two day as rapidly as possible it become evident from the many camp fire which we pass that we be gain on the indian wherever they have encamp we find the print of a woman 's shoe and we conclude that they have with they some white captive this make we all the more anxious to overtake they and general carr accordingly select all he best horse which could stand a hard run and give order for the wagon train to follow as fast as possible while he push ahead on a forced march at the same time i be order to pick out five or six of the best pawnee and go on in advance of the command keep ten or twelve mile ahead on the trail so that when we overtake the indian we could find out the location of they camp and send word to the troops before they come in sight thus afford ample time to arrange a plan for the capture of the village after have go about ten mile in advance of the regiment we begin to move very cautiously as we be now evidently near the indian we look carefully over the summit of the hill before expose ourselves to plain view and at last we discover the village encamp in the sand-hill south of the south platte river at summit spring here i leave the pawnee scout to keep watch while i go back and inform general carr that the indian be in sight the general at once order he man to tighten they saddle and otherwise prepare for action soon all be excitement among the officer and soldier every one be anxious to charge the village i now change my horse for old buckskin joe who have be lead for I thus far and be comparatively fresh act on my suggestion the general make a circuit to the north believe that if the indian have they scout out they would naturally be watch in the direction whence they have come when we have pass the indian and be between they and the platte river we turn to the left and start toward the village by this manoeuver we have avoid discovery by the sioux scout and we be confident of give they a complete surprise keep the command wholly out of sight until we be within a mile of the indian the general halted the advance guard until all close up and then issue a order that when he sound the charge the whole command be to rush into the village as we halt on the top of the hill overlook the camp of the unsuspecting indian general carr call out to he bugler : sound the charge the bugler for a moment become intensely excite and actually forget the note the general again sing out : sound the charge and yet the bugler be unable to obey the command quartermaster hay -- who have obtain permission to accompany the expedition -- be ride near the general and comprehend the dilemma of the man rush up to he jerk the bugle from he hand and sound the charge himself in clear and distinct note as the troops rush forward he throw the bugle away then draw he pistol be among the first man that enter the village the indian have just drive up they horse and be prepare to make a move of the camp when they see the soldier come down upon they a great many of they succeed in jump upon they pony and leave every thing behind they advance out of the village and prepare to meet the charge but upon second thought they quickly conclude that it be useless to try to check we and those who be mount rapidly ride away while the other on foot flee for safety to the neighbor hill we go through they village shooting right and left at everything we see the pawnee the regular soldier and the officer be all mix up together and the sioux be fly in every direction general carr have instruct the command that when they enter the village they must keep a sharp look out for white woman as he be confident the indian have some captive the company which have be order to take possession of the village after its capture soon find two white woman one of whom have while we be in the sand-hills scout the niobrara country the pawnee indian bring into camp one night some very large bone one of which a surgeon of the expedition pronounce to be the thigh-bone of a human be the indian claim that the bone they have find be those of a person belong to a race of people who a long time ago live in this country that there be once a race of man on the earth whose size be about three time that of a ordinary man and they be so swift and powerful that they could run along-side of a buffalo and take the animal in one arm could tear off a leg and eat the meat as they walk these giant deny the existence of a great spirit and when they hear the thunder or see the lightning they laugh at it and say that they be greater than either this so displeased the great spirit that he cause a great rain-storm to come and the water keep rise higher and higher so that it drive those proud and conceited giant from the low grounds to the hill and thence to the mountain but at last even the mountain top be submerge and then those mammoth man be all drown after the flood have subside the great spirit come to the conclusion that he have make man too large and powerful and that he would therefore correct the mistake by create a race of man of smaller size and less strength this be the reason say the indian that modern man be small and not like the giant of old and they claim that this story be a matter of indian history which have be hand down among they from time immemorial as we have no wagon with we at the time this large and heavy bone be find we be oblige to the manner agree upon early one morning in the spring of 1870 the indian who have approach during the night steal some twenty-one head of horse from mr john burke -- a government contractor -- ben
