little friendly advice and tell he that he be release from custody he go on he way a wiser and a poorer man while the owner of the horse and myself return to the fort i pocket the twenty dollar of course some people might think it be not a square way of do business but i do not know any better just then i have several little case of this kind and i become better post on law in the course of time be assist by lieutenant burr reilly of the fifth cavalry who have be educate for a lawyer one evening i be call upon to perform a marriage ceremony the bridegroom be one of the sergeant of the post i have brace up for the occasion by imbibe rather freely of stimulant and when i arrive at the house with a copy of the statute of nebraska which i have recently receive i feel somewhat confused whether my bewilderment be owe to the importance of the occasion and the large assembly or to the effect of loui woodin 's tanglefoot i can not now distinctly remember -- but my suspicion have always be that it be due to the latter cause i look carefully through the statute to find the marriage ceremony but my effort be unsuccessful finally the time come for the knot to be tie i tell the couple to stand up and then i say to the bridegroom : do you take this woman to be you lawful wed wife to support and love she through life i do be the reply then address myself to the bride i say do you take this man to be you lawful wed husband through life to love honor and obey he -lrb- illustration : a wedding ceremony -rrb- i do be she response then join hand say i to both of they i now pronounce you to be man and wife and whomsoever god and buffalo bill have join together let no man put asunder may you live long and prosper aman this conclude the interesting ceremony which be follow by the usual festivity on such occasion i be highly compliment for the elegant and eloquent manner in which i have tie the matrimonial knot during the summer of 1871 professor marsh of yale college come out to mcpherson with a large party of student to have a hunt and to look for fossil professor marsh have hear of the big bone which have be find by the pawnee in the niobrara country and he intend to look for that as well as other bone he accordingly secure the service of major frank north and the pawnee as a escort i be also to accompany the bone-hunter and would have do so have it not be for the fact that just at that time i be order out with a small scout party to go after some indian -lrb- illustration : a ride for life -rrb- the day before the professor arrive at the fort i have be out hunting on the north side of the north platte river near pawnee spring with several companion when we be suddenly attack by indian who wound one of we number john weister we stand the indian off for a little while and weister get even with they by kill one of they party the indian however outnumber we and at last we be force to make a run for we life in this we succeed and reach the fort in safety the general want to have the indian pursue and say he could not spare I to accompany professor marsh however i have the opportunity to make the acquaintance of the eminent professor whom i find to be not only a well-posted person but a very entertaining gentleman he give I a geological history of the country tell I in what section fossil be to be find and otherwise entertain I with several scientific yarn some of which seem too complicated and too mysterious to be believe by a ordinary man like myself but it be all clear to he i ride out with he several mile as he be start on he bone-hunting expedition and i greatly enjoy the ride he party have be provide with government transportation and he student be all mount on government horse as we ride along he deliver a scientific lecture and he convince I that he know what he be talk about i finally bid he good-bye and return to the post while the fossil-hunter be out on they expedition we have several lively little skirmish with the indian after have be absent some little time professor marsh and he party come back with they wagon load down with all kind of bone and the professor be in he glory he have evidently strike a bone-yard and hunting expedition early in the month of September 1871 information be receive at fort mcpherson that general sheridan and a party of invite friend be come out to the post to have a grand hunt in the vicinity and to explore the country from mcpherson to fort hay in kansa on the morning of September 22d they arrive in a special car at north platte a station on the union pacific distant eighteen mile from fort mcpherson the party consist of general sheridan lawrence r jerome jame gordon bennett of the _ new york herald _ leonard w jerome carroll livingston major jg hecksher general fitzhugh general he davy captain m edward rogers colonel j scuyler crosby samuel johnson general anson stager of the western union telegraph company charle wilson editor of the _ chicago evening journal _ general rucker quartermaster-general and dr asch -- the two last-named being of general sheridan 's staff they be meet at the station by general emory and major brown with a cavalry company as escort and a sufficient number of vehicle to carry the distinguished visitor and they baggage a brisk drive of less than two hour over a hard and smooth road bring they to the fort where they find the garrison consist of five company of the fifth cavalry under the command of general carr out on parade await they arrival the band play some martial music and the cavalry pass very handsomely in review before general sheridan the guest be then most hospitably receive and assign to comfortable quarter lieutenant haye the quartermaster of the expedition arrange everything for the comfort of the party one hundred cavalry under command of major brown be detail as a escort a train of sixteen wagon be provide to carry the baggage supplies and forage for the trip and besides these there be three four-horse ambulance in which the gun be carry and in which member of the party who become weary of the saddle might ride and rest at general sheridan 's request i be to accompany the expedition he introduce I to all he friend and give I a good send-off during the afternoon and evening the gentleman be all entertain at the post in a variety of way include dinner and supper party and music and dancing at a late hour they retire to rest in they tent at the camp which they occupy outside the post -- name camp rucker in honor of general rucker at five o'clock next morning a cavalry bugle sound the _ reveille _ and soon all be astir in the camp preparatory to pull out for the first day 's march i rise fresh and eager for the trip and as it be a nobby and high-toned outfit which i be to accompany i determine to put on a little style myself so i dress in a new suit of light buckskin trim along the seam with fringe of the same material and i put on a crimson shirt handsomely ornament on the bosom while on my head i wear a broad _ sombrero _ then mount a snowy white horse -- a gallant stepper -- i ride down from the fort to the camp rifle in hand i feel first-rate that morning and look well the expedition be soon under way we road for ten mile wind through a wooded ravine call cottonwood cañon intersect the high ground or divide as it be call between the platte and republican river upon emerge from the cañon we find ourselves upon the plain first in the line ride general sheridan follow by he guest and then the orderly then come the ambulance in one of which be carry five greyhound bring along to course the antelope and rabbit with the ambulance march a pair of indian pony belong to lieutenant haye -- capture during some indian fight -- and harness to a light wagon which general sheridan occasionally use these little horse but thirteen hand high show more vigor and endurance than any other of the animal we have with we follow the ambulance come the main body of the escort and the supply wagon we march seventeen mile the first day and go into camp on fox creek a tributary of the republican no hunting have as yet be do but i inform the gentleman of the party that we would strike the buffalo country the next day a hundred or more question be then ask I by this one and that one and the whole evening be spend principally in buffalo talk sandwich with story of the plain -- both of war and of the chase several of the party who be good vocalist give we some excellent music we close the evening by christen the camp name it camp brown in honor of the gallant officer in command of the escort at three o'clock next morning the bugle call we to a early start we have breakfast at half-past four and at six be in the saddle all be eager to see and shoot the buffalo which i assure they we would certainly meet during the day after march five mile the advance guard of which i have the command discover six buffalo grazing at a distance of about two mile from we we return to the hunter with this information and they at once consult with I as to the best way to attack the enemy act upon my suggestion fitzhugh crosby lawrence jerome livingston hecksher and roger accompany by myself as guide ride through a convenient cañon to a point beyond the buffalo so that we be to the windward of the animal the rest of the party make a detour of nearly five mile keep behind the crest of a hill we charge down upon the buffalo at full gallop and just then the other party emerge from they concealment and witness the exciting chase the buffalo start off in a line single file fitzhugh after a lively gallop lead we all and soon come alongside the rear buffalo at which he fire the animal falter and then with another shot fitzhugh bring he to the ground crosby dash by he and level another of the herd while livingston drop a third those who be not directly engage in the hunt now come up and congratulate the man upon they success and fitzhugh be at once hail as the winner of the buffalo cup while all sympathize with hecksher whose chance have be the best at the start but who lose by reason of he horse fall and roll over he the hunt be over the column move forward on its march pass through a prairie-dog town several mile in extent these animal be find throughout the plain live together in a sort of society they numberless burrow in they town adjoin each other so that great care be necessary in ride through these place as the ground be so undermine as often to fall in under the weight of a horse around the entrance to they hole the ground be pile up almost a foot high on these little elevation the prairie-dog sit upon they hind leg chatter to each other and observe whatever pass on the plain they will permit a person to approach quite near but when they have view he closely they dive into they den with wonderful quickness they be difficult to kill and if hit generally succeed in crawl underground before they can be capture rattlesnake and small owl be generally find in great number in the prairie-dog town and live in the same hole with the dog on friendly term a few of the prairie-dog be kill and be find to be very palatable eating -lrb- illustration : prairie-dog village -rrb- a short distance beyond the dog town we discover a settlement of five white man who prove to be the two clifford brother arthur ruff dick seymor and john nelson -- the latter already refer to in these page each of they have a squaw wife and numerous half-breed child live in tent of buffalo skin they own a herd of horse and mule and a few cattle and have cultivate a small piece of land they principal occupation be hunting and they have a large number of buffalo hide which they have tan in the indian manner upon reach pleasant valley on medicine creek we party divide into two detachment -- one hunting along the bank of the stream for elk or deer and the other remain with the main body of the escort the elk hunter meet with no success whatever but the other run across plenty of buffalo and nearly everybody kill one or more before the day be over lawrence jerome make a excellent shot while ride in a ambulance he kill a buffalo which attempt to cross the line of march at about four o'clock pm we arrive at mitchell 's fork of the medicine have travel thirty-five mile during that day and there we go into camp -- call it camp jack haye in adventure of the day upon cross the republican river on the morning of the 26th we come upon a immense number of buffalo scatter over the country in every direction as far as the eye could reach and all have a opportunity to do as much hunting as they wish the wagon and troops move slowly along in the direction of the next camp while the hunter go off separately or by two and three in different direction and all be reward with abundant success lawrence jerome however have he career suddenly check he have dismount to make a steady and careful shot and thoughtlessly let go of the bridle the hope of the accuse 's amendment i would defer pronounce sentence the trial afford its considerable amusement and give I a splendid opportunity to display the legal knowledge which i have acquire while act as justice of the peace at fort mcpherson on the morning of the 28th the command cross the south beaver distant nine mile from camp cody and then strike a fair road we make a rapid march until we it be all right as the indian be pawnee unfortunately he do not hear I but keep straight on not stop he horse until he reach the camp -lrb- illustration : mccarthy 's fright -rrb- i know that he would by infantry await the arrival of the third cavalry -lrb- illustration : find the remains of the buck party -rrb- chapter xxv hunting with a grand duke about the first of January 1872 general forsyth and dr asch of sheridan 's staff come out to fort mcpherson to make preparation for a big buffalo hunt for the grand duke alexi of russium and as this be to be no ordinary affair these officer have be send by general sheridan to have all the necessary arrangement perfect by the time the grand duke should arrive they learn from I that there be plenty of buffalo in the vicinity and especially on the red willow sixty mile distant they say they would like to go over on the red willow and pick out a suitable place for the camp they also inquire the location of the spotted tail sioux indian spot tail have permission from the government to hunt the buffalo with he people during the winter in the republican river country it be my opinion that they be located somewhere on the frenchman 's fork about one hundred and fifty mile from fort mcpherson general sheridan 's commissioner inform I that he wish I to visit spotted tail 's camp and induce about one hundred of the lead warrior and chief to come to the point where it should be decide to locate the alexi hunting camp and to be there by the time the grand duke should arrive so that he could see a body of american indian and observe the manner in which they kill buffalo the indian would also be call upon to give a grand war dance in honor of the distinguished visitor next morning general forsyth and dr asch accompany by captain hay who have be leave at fort mcpherson in charge of the fifth cavalry horse take a ambulance and a light wagon to carry they tent and provision sufficient to last they two or three day start under my guidance the post the next day while i leave for spotted tail 's camp the weather be very cold and i find my journey by no mean a pleasant one as i be oblige to camp out with only my saddle blanket and besides there be more or less danger from the indian themselves for although spotted tail himself be friendly i be afraid i might have difficulty in get into he camp i be liable at any moment to run into a in a low ravine i crawl up a high hill where i obtain a good view of the country i could see for four or five mile up the creek and get sight of a village and of two or three hundred pony in its vicinity i wait until night come and then i succeed in ride into the indian camp unobserved -lrb- illustration : spotted tail -rrb- i have see spotted tail 's camp when he come from the north and i know the kind of lodge he be live in as i enter the village i wrap a blanket around my head so that the indian could not tell whether i be a white or a red man in this way i ride around until i find spotted tail 's lodge dismount from my horse i open he tent door and look in and see the old chief lie on some robe i speak to he and he recognize I at once and invite I to enter inside the lodge i find a white man a old frontiersman todd randall who be spotted tail 's agent and who have live a great many year with the indian he understand they language perfectly and do all the interpret for that the next morning he would call he people together and select those who would accompany he i tell spotted tail how i have enter he camp he reply that i have act wisely that although he people be and i find it difficult to hold they they fairly fly over the ground and at last we reach a steep hill or divide which lead down into the valley of the medicine there be no brake on the wagon and the my arm we lay he away to rest in the beautiful cemetery of mount hope amid sorrow and tear chapter xxx i return to the plain we close we theatrical season earlier than usual in the spring of 1876 the indian have not yet cross the creek on my way back to the command i discover a large party of indian which prove to be the cheyenne come up from the south and i hurry to the camp with this which we have come the night before and upon closer observation with we field glass we discover two mount soldier evidently carry dispatch for we push forward on we trail the indian be evidently endeavor to intercept these two man and general merritt fear that they would accomplish they object he do not think it advisable to send out any soldier to the assistance of the courier for fear that answer before the great judge of we all for the death of daring young custer and the boy who round he do fall perhaps i be judge they harshly but i mean what i be tell ye pard i be let they down mighty easy perhaps they may think it be hard but i tell you the day be approach -- the boy be begin to muster -- that day of the great retribution the day of revenge for we custer and i will be with you friend cody my weight will go in with the boy i share all they hardship last winter i share all they sorrow and joy tell they i be come friend william i trust i will meet you ere long regard to the boy in the mountain yours ever in friendship still strong jack be a new man in the country but evidently have plenty of nerve and pluck as he have bring dispatch from fort fetterman a distance of 300 mile through a dangerous indian country the dispatch be for general crook and notify he that general terry be to operate with a large command south of the yellowstone and that the two command would probably consolidate somewhere on the rosebud jack at once hunt I up and give I a letter from general sheridan inform I that he have appoint he -lrb- jack -rrb- as one of the scout while we be converse jack inform I that he have bring I a present from colonel jone of cheyenne and that he have it in he saddle-pocket ask the nature of the gift he reply that it be only a bottle of good whiskey i place my hand over he mouth and tell he to keep still and not to whisper it even to the wind for there be too many dry man around we and only when alone with he do i dare to have he take the treasure from he saddle-pocket in this connection i may remark that jack crawford be the only man i have ever know that could have bring that bottle of whiskey through without _ accident _ befall it for he be one of the very few teetotal scout i ever meet not wish to have a game of whiskey _ solitaire _ i invite general carr to sample the bottle with I we soon find a secluded spot and dismount we think we be go to have a nice little drink all by ourselves when who should ride up but mr lathrop the reporter of the associated press of the pacific slope -- to whom we have give the name of the death rattler -- and who be also know in san francisco as the man with the iron jaw he have with the true nose of a reporter smell the whiskey from afar off and have come to interview it he be a good fellow withal and we be glad to have he join we now to resume : for two or three day we push on but we do not seem to gain much on the indian as they be evidently make about the same march that we be on the fourth or fifth morning of we pursuit i ride ahead of the command about ten mile and mount a hill i scan the country far and wide with my field glass and discover a immense column of dust rise about ten mile further down the creek and soon i notice a body of man march towards I that at first i believe to be the indian of whom we be in pursuit but subsequently they prove to be general terry 's command i send back word to that effect to general crook by a scout who have accompany I but after he have depart i observe a band of indian on the opposite side of the creek and also another party directly in front of I this lead I to believe that i have make a mistake but shortly afterwards my attention be attract by the appearance of a body of soldier who be form into a skirmish line and then i become convinced that it be general terry 's command after all and that the red-skin whom i have see be some of he friendly indian scout who have mistake I for a sioux and flee back to they command terribly excited shout the sioux be come general terry at once come to the post and order the seventh cavalry to form line of battle across the rosebud he also order up he artillery and have they prepare for action doubtless dread another custer massacre i afterwards learn the indian have see the dust raise by general crook 's force and have report that the sioux be come these maneuver i witness from my position with considerable amusement think the command must be badly demoralize when one man could cause a whole army to form line of battle and prepare for action have enjoy the situation to my heart 's content i gallop down towards the skirmish line wave my hat and when within about one hundred yard of the troops colonel weir of the seventh cavalry gallop out and meet I he recognize I at once and accompany I inside the line then he sing out boy here 's buffalo bill some of you old soldier know he give he a cheer thereupon the regiment give three rousing cheer and it be follow up all along the line colonel weir present I to general terry and in answer to he question i inform he that the alarm of indian which have be give be a false one as the dust see by he scout be cause by general crook 's troops general terry thereupon ride forward to meet general crook and i accompany he at he request that night both command go into camp on the rosebud general terry have he wagon train with he and everything to make life comfortable on a indian campaign he have large wall tent and portable bed to sleep in and large hospital tent for dining-room he camp look very comfortable and attractive and present a great contrast to that of general crook who have for he headquarters only one small fly tent and whose cooking utensil consist of a quart cup -- in which he make he coffee himself -- and a stick upon which he broil he bacon when i compare the two camp i come to the conclusion that general crook be a indian fighter for it be evident that he have learn that to follow and fight indian a body of man must travel lightly and not be detain by a wagon train or heavy luggage of any kind that evening general terry order general mile to take he regiment the fifth infantry and return by a forced march to the yellowstone and proceed down that river by steamboat to the mouth of powder river to intercept the indian in case they attempt to cross the yellowstone general mill make a forced march that night of thirty-five mile which be splendid travel for a infantry regiment through a mountainous country general crook and terry spend that evening and the next day in council and on the follow morning both command move out on the indian trail although general terry be the senior officer he do not assume command of both expedition but leave general crook in command of he own troops although they operate together we cross the tongue river to powder river and proceed down the latter stream to a point twenty mile from its junction with the yellowstone where the indian trail turn to the southeast in the direction of the black hill the two command now be nearly out of supplies the trail be abandon and the troops keep on down powder river to its confluence with the yellowstone and remain there several day here we meet general mill who report that no indian have as yet cross the yellowstone several steamboat soon arrive with a large quantity of supplies and once more the boy in blue be make happy chapter xxxi dangerous work one evening while we be in camp on the yellowstone at the mouth of powder river i be inform that the commanding officer have select loui richard a half breed and myself to accompany general mill on a scout expedition on the steamer far west down the yellowstone as far as glendive creek we be to ride on the pilot house and keep a sharp lookout on both side of the river for indian trail that might have cross the stream the idea of scout on a steamboat be indeed a novel one to I and i anticipate a pleasant trip at daylight next morning we report on board the steamer to general mill who have with he four or five company of he regiment we be somewhat surprise when he ask we where we horse be as we have not suppose that horse would be need if the scout be to be do on the steamer he say we might need they before we get back and thereupon we have the animal bring on board in a few minute we be boom down the river at the rate of about twenty mile a hour the steamer far west be command by captain grant marsh whom i find to be a brick i have often hear of he for he be and be yet one of the best know river captain in the country he it be who with he steamer the far west transport the wound man from the battle of the little big horn to fort abraham lincoln on the missourus river and on that trip he make the fastest steamboat time on record he be a skillful and experienced pilot handle he boat with remarkable dexterity while richard and myself be at we station on the pilot house the steamer with a full head of steam go fly past island around bend over sand bar at a rate that be exhilarating presently i think i could see horse grazing in a distant bend of the river and i report the fact to general mill who ask captain marsh if he could land the boat near a large tree which he point out to he -lrb- illustration : scout on a steamboat -rrb- yes sir i can land she there and make she climb the tree if necessary say he on reach the spot designate general mill order two company ashore while richard and myself be order to take we horse off the boat and push out as rapidly as possible to see if there be indian in the vicinity while we be get ashore captain marsh remark that if there be only a good heavy dew on the grass he would shoot the steamer ashore and take we on the scout without the trouble of leave the boat it be a false alarm however as the object we have see prove to be indian grave quite a large number of brave who have probably be kill in some battle have be bury on scaffold accord to the indian custom and some of they clothing have be tear loose from the body by the wolf and be wave in the air on arrive at glendive creek we find that colonel rice and he company of the fifth infantry who have be send there by general mill have build quite a good little fort with they trowel-bayonet -- a weapon which colonel rice be the inventor of and which be by the way a very useful implement of war as it can be use for a shovel in throw up intrenchment and can be profitably utilize in several other way on the day previous to we arrival colonel rice have a fight with a party of indian and have kill two or three of they at long range with he rodman cannon the far west be to remain at glendive over night and general mill wish to send dispatch back to general terry at once at he request i take the dispatch and ride seventy-five mile that night through the bad land of the yellowstone and reach general terry 's camp next morning after have nearly broken my neck a dozen time or more there be but little prospect of any more fighting i determine to go east as soon as possible to organize a new dramatic combination and have a new drama write for I base upon the sioux war this i know would be a pay investment as the sioux campaign have excite considerable interest so i start down the river on the steamer yellowstone _ en route _ to fort beauford on the same morning general terry and crook pull out for powder river to take up the old indian trail which we have recently leave the steamer have proceed down the stream about twenty mile when it be meet by another boat on its way up the river have on board general whistler and some fresh troops for general terry 's command both boat land and almost the first person i meet be my old friend and partner texa jack who have be send out as a dispatch carrier for the _ new york herald _ general whistler upon learn that general terry have leave the yellowstone ask I to carry to he some important dispatch from general sheridan and although i object he insist upon my perform this duty say that it would only detain I a few hour longer as a extra inducement he offer I the use of he own thorough-bred horse which be on the boat i finally consent to go and be soon speed over the rough and hilly country towards powder river and i deliver the dispatch to general terry that same evening general whistler 's horse although a good animal be not use to such hard ride and be far more exhaust by the journey than i be after i have take a lunch general terry ask I if i would carry some dispatch back to general whistler and i reply that i would captain smith general terry 's aid-de-camp offer I he horse for the trip and it prove to be a excellent animal for i ride he that same night forty mile over the bad land in four hour and reach general whistler 's steamboat at one o'clock during my absence the indian have make they appearance on the different hill in the vicinity and the troops from the boat have have several skirmish with they when general whistler have finish read the dispatch he say : cody i want to send information to general terry concern the indian who have be skirmish around here all day i have be try all the evening long to induce some one to carry my dispatch to he but no one seem willing to undertake the trip and i have get to fall back on you it be ask a great deal i know as you have just ridden eighty mile but it be a case of necessity and if you 'll go cody i 'll see that you be well pay for it never mind about the pay say i but get you dispatch ready and i 'll start at once in a few minute he hand I the package and mount the same horse which i have ride from general terry 's camp i strike out for my destination it be two o'clock in the morning when i leave the boat and at eight o'clock i ride into general terry 's camp just as he be about to march -- have make one hundred and twenty mile in twenty-two hour general terry after read the dispatch halt he command and then ride on and overtake general crook with whom he hold a council the result be that crook 's command move on in the direction which they have be pursue while terry 's force march back to the yellowstone and cross the river on steamboat at the urgent request of general terry i accompany the command on a scout in the direction of the dry fork of the missourus where it be expect we would strike some indian the first march out from the yellowstone be make in the night as we wish to get into the hill without be discover by the sioux scout after march three day a little to the east of north we reach the buffalo range and discover fresh sign of indian who have evidently be kill buffalo general terry now call on I to carry dispatch to colonel rice who be still camp at the mouth of glendive creek on the yellowstone -- distant about eighty mile from we night have set in with a storm and a drizzling rain be fall when at ten o'clock i start on this ride through a section of country with which i be entirely unacquainted i travel through the darkness a distance of about thirty-five mile and at daylight i ride into a secluded spot at the head of a ravine where stand a bunch of ash tree and there i conclude to remain till night for i consider it a dangerous undertaking to cross the wide prairie in broad daylight -- especially as my horse be a poor one -lrb- illustration : close quarter -rrb- i accordingly unsaddled my animal and eat a hearty breakfast of bacon and hard tack which i have store in the saddle-pockets then after take a smoke i lay down to sleep with my saddle for a pillow in a few minute i be in the land of dream after sleep some time -- i can not tell how long -- i be suddenly awaken by a roar rumble sound i instantly seize my gun spring to my horse and hurriedly secrete he in the brush then i climb up the steep side of the bank and cautiously look over the summit in the distance i see a large herd of buffalo which be be chase and fire at by twenty or thirty indian occasionally a buffalo would drop out of the herd but the indian keep on until they have kill ten or fifteen they then turn back and begin to cut up they game i saddle my horse and tie he to a small tree where i could reach he conveniently in case the indian should discover I by find my trail and follow it i then crawl carefully back to the summit of the bluff and in a conceal position watch the indian for two hour during which time they be occupy in cut up the buffalo and pack the meat on they pony when they have finish this work they ride off in the direction whence they have come and on the line which i have propose to travel it appear evident to I that they camp be located somewhere between I and glendive creek but i have no idea of abandon the trip on that account i wait till nightfall before resume my journey and then i bear off to the east for several mile and by make a semi-circle to avoid the indian i get back on my original course and then push on rapidly to colonel rice 's camp which i reach just at daylight colonel rice have be fight indian almost every day since he have be encamp at this point and he be very anxious to notify general terry of the fact of course i be request to carry he dispatch after remain at glendive a single day i start back to find general terry and on the third day out i overhaul he at the head of deer creek while on he way to colonel rice 's camp he be not however go in the right direction but bear too far to the east and i so informed he he then ask I to guide the command and i do so on arrive at glendive i bade good-bye to the general and he officer and take passage on the steamer far west which be on she way down the missourus at bismarck i leave the steamer and proceed by rail to rochester new york where i meet my family mr j clinton hall manager of the rochester opera house be very anxious to have I play a engagement at he theater i agree to open the season with he as soon as i have get my drama write and i do so meet with a enthusiastic reception my new drama be arrange for the stage by jv arlington the actor it be a five-act play without head or tail and it make no difference at which act we commence the performance before we have finish the season several newspaper critic i have be tell go crazy in try to follow the plot it afford we however ample opportunity to give a noisy rattle gunpowder entertainment and to present a succession of scene in the late indian war all of which seem to give general satisfaction from rochester i go to new york and play a very successful engagement at the grand opera house under the management of messr poole and donnelly thence my route take I to all the principal city in the eastern western and middle state and i everywhere meet with crowded house i then go to the pacific coast against the advice of friend who give it as they opinion that my style of play would not take very well in californium i open for a engagement of two week at the bush street theater in san francisco at a season when the theatrical business be dull and ben debar and the lingard be play there to empty seat i expect to play to a slim audience on the opening night but instead of that i have a fourteen hundred dollar house such be my success that i continue my engagement for five week and the theater be crowd at every performance upon leave san francisco i make a circuit of the interior town and close the season at virginia city nevada on my way east i meet my family at denver where they be visit my sister nellie and may who be then reside there some time previously i have make arrangement to go into the cattle business in company with my old friend major frank north and while i be in californium he have build we ranch on the south fork of the dismal river sixty-five mile north of north platte in nebraska proceeding to ogalalla the headquarters of the texa cattle drover i find major north there await I and together we buy branded and drive to we ranch we first installment of cattle this occupied we during the remainder of the summer leave the cattle in charge of major north i visit red cloud agency early in the fall and secure some sioux indian to accompany I on my theatrical tour of 1877-78 take my family and the indian with I i go directly to rochester there i leave my oldest daughter arta at a young lady ' seminary while my wife and youngest child travel with I during the season i open at the bowery theater new york September 3d 1877 with a new border drama entitle may cody or lose and win from the pen of major as burt of the united state army it be found on the incident of the mountain meadow massacre and life among the mormon it be the best drama i have yet produce and prove a grand success both financially and artistically the season of 1877-78 prove to be the most profitable one i have ever have in February 1878 my wife become tired of travel and proceed to north platte nebraska where on we farm adjoining the town she personally superintend the erection of a comfortable family residence and have it all complete when i reach there early in may in this house we be now live and we hope to make it we home for many year to come chapter xxxii conclusion after my arrival at north platte i find that the ranchman or cattle-man have organize a regular annual round-up to take place in the spring of the year the word round-up be derive from the fact that during the winter month the cattle become scatter over a vast tract of land and the ranchman assemble together in the spring to sort out and each secure he own stock they form a large circle often of a circumference of two hundred mile and drive the cattle towards a common center where all the stock be brand each owner can readily separate he own from the general herd and then he drive they to he own ranch in this cattle drive business be exhibit some most magnificent horsemanship for the cow-boy as they be call be invariably skillful and fearless horseman -- in fact only a most expert rider could be a cow-boy as it require the greatest dexterity and daring in the saddle to cut a wild steer out of the herd major north be await I upon my arrival at north platte have with he we own horse and man other cattle owner such as keith and barton coe and carter jack pratt the walker brother guy and sim lang arnold and ritchie and a great many other with they outfit be assemble and be ready to start on the round-up my old friend dave perry who have present buckskin joe to I and who reside at north platte be most anxious to go with we for pleasure and frank north tell he he could and have plenty of fun provide he would furnish he own horse provision and bedding and do the usual work require of a cow-boy this dave be willing to undertake we find he to be a good fellow in camp and excellent company as there be nothing but hard work on these round-up have to be in the saddle all day and standing guard over the cattle at night rain or shine i could not possibly find out where the fun come in that north have promise I but it be a exciting life and the day speed rapidly by in six week we find ourselves at we own ranch on dismal river the round-up have prove a great success as we have find all we cattle and drive they home this work be over i propose to spend a few week with my family at north platte for the purpose of make they better acquaintance for my long and continue absence from home make I a comparative stranger under my own roof-tree one great source of pleasure to I be that my wife be delighted with the home i have give she amid the prairie of the far west soon after my arrival my sister nellie and may come to make we a visit and a delightful time we all have during they stay when they leave we i accompany they to they home in denver colorado where i pass several day visit old friend and scene return to ogallala i purchase from bill phant a extensive cattle drover from texa a herd of cattle which i drive to my ranch on the dismal river after which i bade my partner and the boy good-bye and start for the indian territory to procure indian for my dramatic combination for the season of 1878-79 _ en route _ to the territory i pay a long promise visit to my sister julia -- mr ja goodman -- and eliza -- mr george m myer -- who reside in kansa the state which the reader will remember be my boyhood home have secure my indian actor and along with they mr o a burgess a government interpreter and ed a burgess know as the boy chief of the pawnee i start for baltimore where i organize my combination and which be the largest troupe i have yet have on the road opening in that city at the opera house under the management of hon john t ford and then start on a southern tour playing in washington richmond and as far south as savannah georgium where we be bring to a sudden halt owe to the yellow fever which be then cruelly rage in the beautiful city of the land of the cotton and the cane -lrb- illustration : one of the troupe -rrb- while play in washington i suddenly learn from a reporter -- washington newspaper man know everything -- that my indian be to be seize by the government and send back to they agency find that there be foundation for the rumor i at once seek general carl shurz secretary of the interior and ask he if he intend deprive I of my indian actor he say that he do as the indian be away from they reservation without leave i answer that i have have indian with I the year before and nothing have be say about it but commissioner haight reply that the indian be the ward of the government and be not allow off of they reservation i tell the commissioner that the indian be frequently off of they reservation out west as i have a distinct remembrance of meet they upon several occasion on the war path and furthermore i think i be benefit the indian as well as the government by take they all over the united state and give they a correct idea of the custom life etc of the pale face so that when they return to they people they could make know all they have see after a conversation with the secretary of the interior the commissioner conclude to allow I to retain the indian by appoint I indian agent provide i would give the necessary bond and pledge myself to return they in safety to they agency -- which term i agree to from savannah georgium have change my route on account of the yellow fever i jump my entire company to philadelphium and at once continue on a north-eastern tour have arrange with the well-known author and dramatist colonel prentiss ingraham to write a play for I the drama entitle the knight of the plain or buffalo bill 's best trail be first produce at new haven conn it have prove a great success and i expect to play it in england where i purpose to go next season on a theatrical tour have be urge to do so by my many friend abroad after a successful tour of six week on the pacific slope thus end the season of 1878-79 i be at my home at north platte nebraska for the summer and thus end the account of my career as far as it have go the end end of the project gutenberg ebook of the life of hon william f cody by william f cody
